# FastDB-First CRM ABI And Resource Bridge Plan

> **Status:** Superseded for integration-boundary purposes by `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-20-c-two-fastdb-first-contract-boundary-redesign.md`
> **Date:** 2026-05-18
> **Scope:** Make fastdb the required portable CRM payload ABI for cross-language C-Two contracts, while keeping Python-native CRM annotations available only for Python-only prototype and test flows.

## Closure Boundary

As of 2026-05-20, this plan is historical migration evidence. Its older language about FastDB-owned C-Two provider/codegen surfaces and C-Two being fastdb-neutral is superseded. The current boundary is that C-Two contract layers own FastDB-backed CRM planning, bridge derivation, codegen, typed facades, and cross-transport verification, while C-Two runtime route/relay/IPC/scheduler/lease/lifecycle layers do not parse FastDB storage internals.

As of 2026-05-20, this workstream should stop adding incremental bridge-shape guardrails inside the current goal. The bounded closure scope is the fastdb-first portable CRM ABI, FastDB-owned call-db provider and bridge planning, C-Two codec-neutral descriptors/diagnostics/codegen, bridge execution across thread-local/direct IPC/explicit HTTP relay paths, held FastDB call-db views, and the initial TypeScript HTTP/direct-IPC/c2-mem-ffi proof. The remaining items in Implementation Order item 91 are follow-up workstreams, not blockers for this bounded closure.

Do not continue the phase loop only to add aliases for already-covered bridge families unless a real resource shape exposes a production bug or an unsupported behavior needs an explicit fail-fast guardrail. Future work should start from a separate plan with its own acceptance criteria for broader real IPC coverage, publishable TypeScript SDK packaging, Bun/Deno or equivalent native/FFI loaders, TypeScript runtime coverage for non-native variable-length layouts, broad arbitrary bridge synthesis, or lower-level fixed-table/heap-backed column writes backed by benchmark evidence.

## Decision

Portable C-Two CRM contracts should use `c-two.contract.v1` for callable resource identity and fastdb call-db codecs for method input and output payload ABI. C-Two still does not parse fastdb feature schemas, call-db tables, engine profiles, or native storage internals; it records and validates opaque `CodecRef` values, routes calls, owns leases, and invokes provider-generated transfer adapters.

Python-native annotations may remain useful for local experiments and Python-only tests, but they are not a portable contract path. When a CRM method resolves to `python-pickle-default`, normal Python execution can continue, while portable export, strict codegen, and cross-language SDK generation must emit diagnostics or fail rather than silently treating that method as portable.

The missing piece between a fastdb CRM ABI and existing resource implementations is an explicit resource bridge. If a resource method already accepts and returns fastdb-native values, the bridge is identity. If the resource method is written against existing Python/Pandas/GIS structures, registration must install or derive a bridge that converts fastdb CRM inputs into resource inputs before the method call and converts resource outputs back into fastdb CRM outputs after the call.

## Core Invariants

| Invariant | Regression prevented | Verification target |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Portable CRM wire refs are fastdb call-db refs or no-payload refs, never pickle refs. | Cross-language clients accidentally depending on Python pickle or Python class importability. | `build_portable_contract_descriptor`, `export_contract_descriptor`, Rust contract validation, strict codegen tests, descriptor scans for `python-pickle-default`. |
| C-Two core remains fastdb-neutral. | Python SDK or Rust core importing fastdb internals and forcing future SDKs to duplicate Python behavior. | Import scan showing no top-level fastdb imports under C-Two core/SDK except tests/examples/docs. |
| Bridge conversion applies on every execution path. | Thread-local same-process calls bypassing the fastdb ABI while IPC/relay use it, causing different semantics and missed zero-copy behavior. | Tests covering thread-local, direct IPC, and relay for a bridged CRM/resource pair. |
| Bridge identity is explicit and cheap for fastdb-native resources. | High-performance resources paying unnecessary materialization/conversion cost. | Tests for no-op bridge planning plus focused micro guardrails around view-backed returns. |
| Normal calls return ergonomic owning values, while `cc.hold(...)` returns retained fastdb views where the provider can safely expose them. | Hidden behavior changes in ordinary calls and hidden copies in high-performance held calls. | Hold tests assert `from_buffer` path, retained lease release, view invalidation after release, and no `bytes(memoryview)` copy in held columnar view creation. |
| fastdb owns scalar, single feature, array, batch, and graph planning. | C-Two learning fastdb table/engine rules or downstream users needing new C-Two types for every fastdb feature. | fastdb planner tests for scalar, `Feature`, `Array[T]`, `Batch[T]`, tuple returns, and object-graph profile selection. |
| Provider failure is explicit before portable export. | Half-fastdb methods falling through to pickle and only failing after deployment or codegen. | Negative tests where missing fastdb provider, unsupported nested data, or unsupported graph profile produces actionable diagnostics. |

## Source-To-Sink Matrix

| Path | Producer | Storage/cache | Network/wire | FFI/SDK boundary | Consumer | Test/support risk | Legacy/bypass guardrail |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| CRM contract identity | `@cc.crm(namespace=..., version=...)` and descriptor builder | CRM class attributes and Rust route contract metadata | IPC handshake and relay route metadata carry contract hashes | Python exporter and PyO3/Rust `c2-contract` validation must see the same descriptor | Python proxy, Rust route validation, codegen | Test helpers that build descriptors directly can omit route registration | Hash must include method wire refs; route matching cannot degrade to name-only resolution. |
| FastDB call-db input | fastdb provider plans a method input from CRM context and annotations | Generated transferable on wrapped CRM method; fastdb sidecar schema descriptor | Serialized as one request payload across IPC/HTTP relay; thread-local must enter same bridge plan | Python provider returns adapter, C-Two core stores only `CodecRef`; future SDKs consume sidecar fastdb schemas | Resource-side transfer wrapper, then bridge input conversion | Unit tests that assert only `_input_transferable` can miss portable export failure | Missing provider or unsupported shape must not silently become portable pickle. |
| Resource bridge input | Registration builds per-method bridge plan | Native server slot or Python slot metadata, shared by local and remote dispatch | No separate network artifact; applied after request decode | Python registration passes bridge plan to Python server slot without Rust parsing fastdb | Resource method | Thread-local tests can pass while remote path uses bridge, or the reverse | Direct calls must not use `CRMProxy.call_direct` to bypass bridge when CRM/resource shapes differ. |
| Resource bridge output | Resource method returns domain value | Per-method bridge plan | Serialized as fastdb call-db output payload across IPC/HTTP relay | Python server dispatch applies bridge before returning bytes or buffer-protocol data to Rust response allocator | Client transfer wrapper or held view constructor | Tests that call resource methods directly can bypass output bridge | Output bridge must run before serialization; errors map to resource execution or serialization boundaries consistently. |
| Held fastdb output | Rust response lease and fastdb provider `from_buffer` | Native retained-buffer lease tracker plus `HeldResult` | IPC/relay response payload can be inline, SHM, handle, or chunked; lease ownership remains Rust-owned | PyO3 memoryview must remain retained until `HeldResult.release()`; SDKs must not copy retained buffers in view constructors | Client `cc.hold(...)`, `FastdbCallView`, table/array/batch views | Materialized decode tests can hide retained-buffer copies | `from_buffer` failure releases lease immediately; view use after release fails; provider must avoid materializing retained buffers unless the plan says the result is owning. |
| Python-only fallback | `create_default_transferable` in auto-transfer | Generated Python default transferable | Python pickle payload only | Python SDK only; no cross-language SDK should receive it as portable | Python runtime only | Nonportable descriptor tests can normalize pickle as acceptable | Descriptor export and strict codegen must reject; diagnostics must say prototype-only, not portable. |

## Current Code Evidence Snapshot

The current c-two code already passes CRM context into `auto_transfer` from `sdk/python/src/c_two/crm/meta.py`, and `auto_transfer` already asks method-level providers before falling back to default pickle transferables in `sdk/python/src/c_two/crm/transferable.py`.

The current descriptor path already exposes a sharp choke point: `_wire_ref_for_input` and `_wire_ref_for_output` fall back to `python-pickle-default`, while portable mode rejects that wire ref in `_ensure_portable_wire_ref` in `sdk/python/src/c_two/crm/descriptor.py`.

The current execution path now has an initial codec-neutral resource bridge. `sdk/python/src/c_two/crm/bridge.py` exposes `cc.bridge(input=..., output=...)`, `sdk/python/src/c_two/crm/conformance.py` accepts annotation or parameter mismatches only for the bridged direction, and `sdk/python/src/c_two/transport/server/native.py` wraps the registered resource once so thread-local direct calls, direct IPC dispatch, and explicit HTTP relay dispatch use the same bridged resource object. The initial fastdb grid smoke uses this bridge against the existing `NestedGrid` resource; fastdb can now derive the grid bridge automatically for scalar/`Array` inputs, single `Feature` inputs to resource `dict[...]` parameters, keyword-constructible domain object parameters, field-tuple or bare-tuple parameters, or name-matched split scalar parameters, `Batch[Feature]` inputs to resource `list[dict[...]]`, `list[DomainObject]`, row-tuple parameters, tuple-column parameters, `dict[str, list[...]]` column mappings, table-object constructors or row-record factory methods, or multiple name-matched `list[...]` parameters, single `Feature` outputs from dict/domain object/field-tuple or bare-tuple returns, and object-list, row-tuple, tuple-column, table-like row-record objects, or `dict[str, list[...]]` column `Batch` outputs, while fastdb-native resource methods with identical fastdb ABI annotations are skipped as no-op bridge methods. The object-list and row-tuple `Batch` output paths and public `object_batch_mapper(...)` helper now reject scalar string/bytes values, single mapping values, non-tuple rows, and wrong row arity as malformed batches before field mapping starts; tuple/dict column `Batch` outputs and `batch_from_columns(...)` reject scalar string/bytes/memoryview values and mappings as malformed columns before column materialization; scalar `Array` bridge helpers reject mappings before Python can iterate mapping keys as array elements; `Batch[Feature]` input bridges normalize table-like row-record exporters before row-field lookup and still reject scalar strings, bytes-like values, single mappings, and non-iterables at the batch boundary. Broader held-view optimization and broader bridge derivation patterns remain future slices.

The current fastdb side already has `fastdb.call-db.schema.v1`, `org.fastdb.call-db`, materialized call-db encode/decode, held `FastdbCallView` for scalar/single-feature/table/array access over columnar output buffers, public `Array[T]` / `Batch[T]` CRM ABI markers for columnar scalar arrays and feature batches, explicit fastdb scalar-only call-db policy, explicit nullable call-db rejection, dependency-neutral bridge conversion helpers, initial automatic bridge derivation including single `Feature` input-to-resource-`dict[...]` / `Mapping[...]` / `MutableMapping[...]`, keyword-constructible domain-object, field-tuple, bare-tuple, or split-scalar conversion, `Batch[Feature]` input-to-resource-`list[dict[...]]`, `Sequence[Mapping[...]]` / `MutableSequence[MutableMapping[...]]`, `list[DomainObject]`, row-tuple, tuple-column, table-object construction from row records, `dict[str, list[...]]` / `Mapping[str, Sequence[...]]` / `MutableMapping[str, MutableSequence[...]]` column-mapping, or split-column `list[...]` / `Sequence[...]` / `MutableSequence[...]` parameter conversion, single `Feature` output conversion from dict/mapping/mutable-mapping/domain object/field-tuple or bare-tuple returns, and object-list, row-tuple, table-like row-record, tuple-column, or dict/mapping/mutable-mapping column `Batch` output conversion, plus call-db `Array[Scalar]` producer-side input/output serialization from ordinary non-mapping, non-bytes-like iterables and call-db `Batch[Feature]` producer-side serialization from table-like row-record exporters such as `to_dict("records")`, `to_dicts()`, or `to_pylist()`, an initial object-graph call-db profile with dependency closure hashing, TypeScript helper generation, fastdb4ts runtime helpers for generated columnar feature/call-db bindings, fastdb4ts runtime helpers for generated object-graph feature and scalar/array/feature-table object-graph call-db bindings, single-`BYTES` columnar feature runtime support, native numeric scalar `list[...]` columnar field runtime support, Python capability/call-db/codegen guardrails that keep non-native scalar list fields such as `list[STR]` and nested list fields such as `list[list[I32]]` semantic-only until fastdb has a concrete variable-length list runtime layout, direct Python engine guardrails that prevent those same non-native lists from falling through to `float64` list storage in `LayerSchema`, `ColumnEngine`, `ObjectEngine`, low-level push/read helpers, or call-db table construction, direct Python raw-payload guardrails that reject multiple `BYTES` fields and route single `BYTES` dynamic tables through raw/Any geometry, a measured fastdb4ts mutable bulk append path for numeric/boolean columnar call-db tables, fastdb4ts Point/Tx32 table geometry for normal feature tables with raw-geometry preservation for single-`BYTES` payload tables, explicit-close TypeScript columnar call-db views, explicit-close TypeScript object-graph call-db views for materialized row/scalar/array/feature access, a single-copy fastdb4ts WASM owned-heap load path for `ORM.fromBuffer(...)`, C-Two call-db views, object-graph call-db views, and `FastSerializer.loads(...)`, a generated `createFastdbC2CodecRegistry()` adapter that can plug these helpers into C-Two's generated codec-aware TypeScript client transport, and a generated typed client facade that wraps C-Two's schema-neutral `unknown` client methods with fastdb schema-derived parameter and return types. C-Two TypeScript codegen now emits required portable `fingerprints` for route ABI/signature hashes, method wire specs, `C2EncodedClientTransport`, a codec transport factory keyed by the same codec identity fields, an explicit HTTP relay data-plane transport that sends Rust relay-compatible expected CRM headers, and an initial relay-aware HTTP transport that performs contract-scoped `/_resolve`, validates resolved route contract identity and positive `max_payload_size`, skips candidates whose advertised `max_payload_size` cannot carry the encoded request payload, and retries only Rust-compatible stale-route responses (`404 ResourceNotFound` or `502 UpstreamUnavailable`) rather than ordinary 500s; allocator-backed HTTP data-plane responses stream known-length bodies directly into provider-owned memory, generated inline and chunked IPC success replies can copy into provider-owned memory after rejecting oversized declared frame payload lengths before payload reads, generated IPC SHM success replies can use explicit `responseShmReader.read(block, destination?)` and `responseShmReader.release(block)` hooks to fill provider-owned allocator views or generated owned-byte destinations after buddy metadata validation and release successfully read blocks, generated IPC request-side SHM writer hooks can advertise client SHM metadata and send large request payloads as Rust-compatible buddy call frames, generated dedicated-only Node/POSIX helpers can read/release dedicated response segments and create/release dedicated request segments over an injected file-system contract, and HTTP can opt into a bounded buffered unknown-length fallback controlled by `responsePayloadUnknownLengthMaxBytes` that snapshots chunks before allocating the exact final size, while all declared `Content-Length` response paths reject values above `2_147_483_647` before allocator calls, body stream reads, or `arrayBuffer()` materialization. `--strict-codecs` accepts fastdb call-db method refs and rejects raw fastdb feature refs as non-CRM method envelopes. It does not yet provide complete TypeScript SDK transport parity such as broader real IPC coverage and publishable packaging beyond the initial Node/POSIX UDS connector smoke, initial `c2-mem-ffi` loader, and initial generated direct IPC grid smoke with c2-mem-ffi request/response SHM in allocator-backed and no-allocator response modes, Bun/Deno or equivalent bindings over the same Rust-owned substrates, browser/runtime packaging guidance, true external-buffer TypeScript zero-copy beyond the current copy-into-WASM boundary for arbitrary JS buffers, broad arbitrary bridge synthesis, or broader TypeScript columnar field coverage for non-native variable-length list layouts; lower-level fixed-table or heap-backed writes remain future work only when benchmarks prove they beat mutable bulk append for C-Two call-db shapes.

Fixed tuple CRM returns are now covered by the FastDB-owned bridge derivation when each tuple item can be satisfied by an existing output mapper. The implementation keeps C-Two neutral by producing ordinary `cc.bridge(output=...)` hooks: it rejects variadic tuple returns, validates typed resource tuple arity during derivation, validates runtime tuple length before response serialization, and maps each item independently through scalar, `Array`, single-feature, or `Batch` output conversion.

Table-like `Batch[Feature]` outputs are now covered by the FastDB-owned bridge derivation when a resource returns an object with row-record export methods such as `to_dict("records")`, `to_dicts()`, or `to_pylist()`, including table-like objects that expose row records but are not themselves iterable. The normalization happens inside FastDB's object-batch helper before generic iteration so pandas-style objects do not get misread as column-name iterables, while custom row iterables with unrelated `to_dict()` methods still take the old row iteration path.

Phase 48 adds the first generated TypeScript held-call path: C-Two emits `C2HeldResult`, `C2HeldClientTransport`, per-method `hold_<method>(...)` wrappers, and codec-transport `hold(...)` implementations that use `codec.fromBuffer(...)` when present and release only those provider-owned views by calling `release()` or `close()` on held values. If a held call falls back to `decode(...)`, release is intentionally a no-op for the materialized value, so arbitrary decoded objects are not closed by naming convention. This does not change the wire protocol and does not claim true external-buffer zero-copy for fastdb4ts; current FastDB views still import HTTP `Uint8Array` payloads into WASM once before exposing explicit-close DB views.

FastDB call-db input transferables deliberately opt out of C-Two automatic input hold when their `from_buffer` hook materializes values instead of returning a resource-facing retained view. Raw fastdb feature transferables use the same opt-out for the same reason. The grid fastdb direct IPC guardrail now proves `get_grid_infos` uses view-mode input handling and leaves no active `resource_input` lease after a real call, while output held calls continue to expose retained fastdb views.

## Public API Direction

The portable CRM should be written in terms of fastdb ABI types and fastdb feature classes. The intended user model is:

```python
import c_two as cc
import fastdb4py as fdb

@fdb.feature
class GridId:
    level: fdb.I32
    global_id: fdb.I32

@fdb.feature
class GridAttribute:
    level: fdb.I32
    global_id: fdb.I32
    center_x: fdb.F64
    center_y: fdb.F64

@cc.crm(namespace="examples.grid", version="0.1.0")
class Grid:
    def get_grid_infos(self, level: fdb.I32, global_ids: fdb.Array[fdb.I32]) -> fdb.Batch[GridAttribute]:
        ...
```

If the resource implementation is already fastdb-native, registration can remain simple:

```python
cc.register(Grid, FastdbGrid(), name="examples/grid")
```

If the resource implementation still uses existing Python/Pandas structures, registration supplies bridge functions:

```python
cc.register(
    Grid,
    NestedGrid(),
    name="examples/grid",
    bridge={
        "get_grid_infos": cc.bridge(
            input=grid_infos_input_to_resource,
            output=grid_infos_output_to_fastdb,
        ),
    },
)
```

`cc.bridge(...)` is now the initial C-Two bridge API. Registration validates bridge method coverage, attaches the bridge plan to the resource object used by remote and thread-local paths, and still fails if an unbridged CRM/resource mismatch is present. Directional guardrails matter: an input hook only relaxes input parameter/annotation conformance, an output hook only relaxes return conformance, and an empty bridge does not bypass validation.

## Client Semantics

Ordinary calls should return owning/materialized values matching the CRM annotation shape: scalar values become ordinary language values, single features become owning feature objects, arrays become owning array values, batches become owning batch/table values, and tuple returns preserve tuple shape.

Held calls should return `HeldResult` and expose view-backed values when fastdb can safely build them from the retained response buffer. For `fdb.Batch[T]`, `.value` should be a batch/table view; for `fdb.Array[T]`, `.value` should be an array view; for a single feature, `.value` may be a row/feature view if fastdb supports it without copying. `HeldResult.release()` remains the owner of lifetime release, and all views must reject use after release.

The fallback behavior for methods without a provider remains Python-only. `cc.hold(...)` may still return a materialized value when no `from_buffer` is available, but that path is not portable and must not appear in strict exported contracts.

## Implementation Order

1. Implemented: tighten C-Two portable contract diagnostics around fastdb-first policy, including development descriptor diagnostics for Python-only methods, provider method diagnostics for fastdb call-db non-claims, strict portable export failure on pickle, and strict TypeScript codegen acceptance only for supported fastdb refs or no-payload refs.
2. Implemented initial slice: add C-Two bridge planning and registration support with per-method bridge metadata, directional conformance rules, and a shared bridged resource path for thread-local/direct IPC/explicit HTTP relay execution.
3. Implemented initial slice: add fastdb public `Array[T]` / `Batch[T]` ABI typing and planner support for columnar scalar arrays and feature batches; CRM-level `list[Feature]` is now rejected with diagnostics that point to `Batch[Feature]`.
4. Implemented initial slice: add fastdb-specific bridge helper builders that make grid conversions concise while keeping C-Two core fastdb-neutral.
5. Implemented initial slice: add fastdb object-graph call-db profile after columnar call-db is stable, including dependency closure hashing, ref/list-ref round-trip, and honest held-call fallback to materialized values because object-graph call-db does not yet claim `buffer-view`.
6. Implemented initial smoke: add a fastdb grid contract where `get_grid_infos` uses `fdb.I32 + fdb.Array[fdb.I32] -> fdb.Batch[GridAttribute]`; `get_active_grid_infos` returns a fastdb GridId batch, with bridges to the existing `NestedGrid` resource and tests for thread-local, direct IPC, explicit HTTP relay, and direct IPC hold view.
7. Implemented initial slice: require explicit fastdb scalar aliases for portable call-db, reject nullable call-db annotations, and let Python builtin scalar methods fall back to C-Two Python-only pickle paths.
8. Implemented initial slice: add fastdb-owned automatic bridge derivation for scalar/`Array` input conversion including `Array[Scalar]` input-to-resource-`tuple[Scalar, ...]` or bare-`tuple` conversion, single `Feature` input-to-resource-`dict[...]`, keyword-constructible domain-object, field-tuple, bare-tuple, or split-scalar conversion, `Batch[Feature]` input-to-resource-`list[dict[...]]` or `list[DomainObject]` conversion, `Batch[Feature]` input-to-tuple-column resource conversion, `Batch[Feature]` input-to-`dict[str, list[...]]` column mappings, `Batch[Feature]` input-to-name-matched split `list[...]` resource parameters, single `Feature` output conversion from dict/domain object/field-tuple or bare-tuple returns, and object-list, tuple-column, or `dict[str, list[...]]` column output conversion to `Batch[Feature]`; grid `fastdb_bridge.py` now uses `derive_c_two_bridge(...)` instead of hand-written per-method converters.
9. Implemented initial slice: wire provider-specific TypeScript/WASM runtime helpers behind generated fastdb helper bindings for columnar feature and columnar call-db payloads, including schema `value_position` metadata so generated call-db bindings can reconstruct argument and return order.
10. Implemented initial slice: expose fastdb held call-db feature table column access for C-Two `cc.hold(...)` users so the grid `get_active_grid_infos` direct IPC smoke can read `return_0` through fastdb columns without materializing the response buffer.
11. Implemented initial performance and codegen smoke slice: fastdb4ts columnar call-db encode now avoids `ORM.push(...)` for numeric/boolean scalar/array/batch tables through a measured mutable bulk append path, FastDB has a generated helper runtime smoke, and C-Two grid's real exported descriptor is checked against fastdb TypeScript helper generation.
12. Implemented clean-cut slice: remove the obsolete automatic portable control-codec transferable path from C-Two; Python-native primitive/container CRM annotations now always resolve to `python-pickle-default`, diagnostics report `python_only_pickle`, portable export rejects them, and Rust TypeScript codegen no longer treats any non-fastdb codec as an implicit built-in runtime.
13. Implemented object-graph TypeScript runtime slices: generated helper/runtime paths now support ObjectEngine-compatible object-graph feature payloads, scalar/array/feature-table object-graph call-db payloads, and explicit-close object-graph call-db views for materialized row/scalar/array/feature access without column access.
14. Implemented guardrail: make automatic bridge derivation no-op for resource methods that already use the same fastdb ABI annotations as the CRM, so high-performance fastdb-native resources do not pay bridge materialization costs.
15. Implemented codegen composition smoke: the real C-Two grid fastdb descriptor now feeds fastdb TypeScript helper generation, compiles with `tsc`, runs under Node, exercises encode/decode/view, and fails if numeric/boolean call-db helpers fall back to `ORM.push(...)`.
16. Implemented initial slice: add fastdb4ts explicit-close columnar call-db views through generated binding `.view(payload)` / `viewFastdbC2CallDb(...)`, including scalar, single-feature, table, array, materialized, and numeric column access guarded by `.close()`.
17. Implemented bridge derivation slice: add `Batch[Feature]` CRM input-to-resource tuple-column conversion for existing column-vector resource methods, with non-list tuple column and wrong tuple length derivation guardrails plus thread-local/direct IPC/explicit HTTP relay integration coverage.
18. Implemented bridge derivation slice: add single `Feature` CRM input-to-resource `dict[...]` conversion for existing dictionary-shaped resource methods, with missing-field guardrails plus thread-local/direct IPC/explicit HTTP relay integration coverage.
19. Implemented bridge derivation slice: add `Batch[Feature]` CRM input-to-resource `list[dict[...]]` conversion for existing dictionary-list resource methods, with missing-field and single-mapping guardrails plus thread-local/direct IPC/explicit HTTP relay integration coverage.
20. Implemented bridge derivation slice: add single `Feature` CRM input-to-domain-object and `Batch[Feature]` CRM input-to-`list[DomainObject]` conversion for resource methods whose domain constructors accept fastdb feature fields as keyword arguments, with constructor-mismatch derivation guardrails plus thread-local/direct IPC/explicit HTTP relay integration coverage.
21. Implemented bridge derivation slice: add `Batch[Feature]` CRM input expansion into multiple resource `list[...]` parameters whose names match fastdb feature fields, with non-list and ambiguous-name derivation guardrails plus thread-local/direct IPC/explicit HTTP relay integration coverage.
22. Implemented bridge derivation slice: add `Batch[Feature]` CRM output conversion from resource `dict[str, list[...]]` column mappings, with non-list dict annotation and missing-column guardrails plus thread-local/direct IPC/explicit HTTP relay integration coverage.
23. Implemented bridge derivation slice: add `Batch[Feature]` CRM input conversion to a resource `dict[str, list[...]]` column mapping, with non-list dict annotation, single-mapping-as-batch, and missing-field guardrails plus thread-local/direct IPC/explicit HTTP relay integration coverage.
24. Implemented TypeScript owned-heap import slice: fastdb4ts now loads `ORM.fromBuffer(...)`, C-Two columnar/object-graph call-db views, and `FastSerializer.loads(...)` by copying external JS bytes into WASM once and transferring that heap buffer to `FastVectorDb` ownership, avoiding the previous extra C++ `malloc+memcpy` in the old `WxDatabase.loadFromHeap(...)` internal path.
25. Implemented non-native scalar list guardrail: fastdb can export semantic `list[STR]`-style schema descriptors, but columnar/object-graph capability, call-db planning, C-Two wrapper diagnostics, and TypeScript helper generation reject these layouts until a real native or auxiliary variable-length list runtime exists.
26. Implemented TypeScript table-layout and encode-performance guardrail slice: fastdb4ts ORM table creation now uses Point/Tx32 geometry for normal feature tables, keeps raw geometry for single-`BYTES` payload tables, large numeric/boolean C-Two call-db payloads round-trip without fixed-table detours, and fixed-table or heap-backed write work remains benchmark-gated because the rechecked detour did not beat mutable bulk append.
27. Implemented TypeScript codec-transport composition slice: C-Two generates required portable `fingerprints`, method wire specs, `C2EncodedClientTransport`, `create{CRM}ClientCodecTransport(...)`, `createHttpRelayEncodedTransport(...)` for explicit relay data-plane bytes calls with expected CRM headers, and `createRelayAwareHttpEncodedTransport(...)` for contract-scoped relay resolve plus Rust-compatible stale-route retry; FastDB generates `createFastdbC2CodecRegistry()` with the same sorted codec requirement key; `--strict-codecs` is intentionally limited to `org.fastdb.call-db` method envelopes and rejects raw feature codecs such as `org.fastdb.columnar`.
28. Implemented bridge guardrail slice: object-list `Batch[Feature]` output bridges and the public `object_batch_mapper(...)` helper now reject scalar string/bytes values and single mapping values as malformed batches, preventing accidental iteration over characters or mapping keys before field validation.
29. Implemented bridge guardrail slice: tuple-column and `dict[str, list[...]]` `Batch[Feature]` output bridges now share `batch_from_columns(...)` column-shape validation, rejecting scalar string/bytes/memoryview values and mappings before they can be split into characters, bytes, or mapping keys.
30. Implemented artifact-bundle codegen closure slice: C-Two exports provider-owned codec artifact bundles through a codec-neutral `export_contract_codec_artifacts(...)` / `c3 contract artifacts` path, FastDB attaches call-db descriptors plus root and dependency feature schema descriptors to generated transferables, FastDB codegen accepts either individual schema descriptors or a JSON artifact bundle, and the grid cross-generated smoke now consumes exported artifacts instead of hand-replanning sidecar schemas in the test.
31. Implemented CLI source-to-sink guardrail: the grid FastDB smoke now proves `c3 contract export`, `c3 contract artifacts`, `c3 contract validate`, and `fdb codegen --c-two-ts --schema <artifact-bundle>` compose through real subprocess commands and the local FastDB provider bundle, not only through in-process Python helper calls.
32. Implemented TypeScript held-call codegen slice: generated clients now expose per-method `hold_<method>(...)` wrappers, generated codec transports implement `C2HeldClientTransport.hold(...)`, and held responses prefer provider `fromBuffer(...)` so FastDB generated registries can return explicit-close `FastdbC2CallDbView` values through C-Two's generated TypeScript client.
33. Implemented FastDB direct-engine non-native list guardrail slice: semantic `list[STR]` export remains allowed, but FastDB no longer creates numeric `list_plan` fallback entries or lets direct `ColumnEngine` / `ObjectEngine` / call-db helper paths push those fields into runtime storage before failing with unrelated NumPy/C++ errors.
34. Implemented TypeScript typed facade slice: FastDB codegen wraps C-Two's generated unknown-return client with provider-owned method parameter, materialized return, and held return types derived from `fastdb.call-db.schema.v1`.
35. Implemented FastDB raw-payload direct-engine guardrail slice: multiple `BYTES` fields are rejected by both capability profiles and direct runtime construction, single `BYTES` dynamic tables round-trip through raw/Any geometry, and the complex inlined push fallback is covered by two-row push tests.
36. Implemented FastDB nested-list semantic guardrail slice: `fastdb.schema.v1` can now describe nested language-native list fields such as `list[list[I32]]`, while capability checks, call-db planning, direct engines, and TypeScript helper generation reject them as non-runnable until FastDB has an auxiliary variable-length list layout.
37. Implemented FastDB call-db `value_position` ABI guardrail slice: schema production, Python runtime value mapping, TypeScript helper generation, fastdb4ts binding validation, and the TypeScript value-count sink all require positions to be present, non-negative, unique, and contiguous from zero before method arguments or returns can be mapped.
38. Implemented FastDB call-db method identity runtime guardrail slice: schema production, Python runtime entrypoints, and fastdb4ts hand-built binding validation now require a non-empty method name and a direction of `input` or `output`, complementing the existing sidecar/contract wire-usage check in FastDB TypeScript helper generation.
39. Implemented FastDB call-db table-name ABI guardrail slice: schema production, Python runtime entrypoints including retained views, TypeScript helper generation, and fastdb4ts hand-built binding validation require non-empty unique table names before payload tables can be addressed.
40. Implemented FastDB call-db profile identity guardrail slice: schema production, Python runtime entrypoints, Python retained-view capability checks, and fastdb4ts hand-built binding encode/decode/view entrypoints reject profiles outside `fastdb.call.columnar.v1` and `fastdb.call.object-graph.v1`.
41. Implemented FastDB call-db CRM context identity guardrail slice: schema production and FastDB TypeScript helper generation accept no CRM context for standalone fastdb plans or a complete non-empty namespace/name/version block for C-Two-shaped plans, but reject partial CRM context before it can become schema identity.
42. Implemented FastDB call-db field-metadata guardrail slice: schema production, Python runtime entrypoints, direct table descriptor generation when runtime feature metadata is available, FastDB TypeScript helper generation, and fastdb4ts hand-built binding validation reject malformed scalar field names/kinds, malformed array item names/kinds, and Python scalar/array kind metadata that is syntactically valid but does not match the runtime dynamic feature annotations.
43. Implemented FastDB call-db feature-schema metadata guardrail slice: schema production, Python runtime entrypoints, direct table descriptor generation, FastDB TypeScript helper generation, and fastdb4ts hand-built binding validation reject feature table schema/dependency metadata that does not match runtime feature types, hash-referenced schemas, or the selected object-graph-only dependency model.
44. Implemented FastDB schema-artifact ref-target guardrail slice: FastDB TypeScript helper generation rejects `ref` / `list[ref]` targets without stable identity/name metadata or with target metadata that disagrees with the supplied referenced schema descriptor, covering both raw feature codec artifacts and call-db method artifacts.
45. Implemented C-Two strict TypeScript codegen guardrail slice: `--strict-codecs` now rejects malformed `org.fastdb.call-db` wire refs that omit `schema="fastdb.call-db.schema.v1"`, use another schema, or omit `schema_sha256`, instead of accepting them solely by codec id and generating unsatisfiable provider requirements.
46. Implemented FastDB codec requirement key guardrail slice: FastDB TypeScript helper generation now preserves optional `media_type` in provider bindings, collects codec requirements and call-db wire source usage with the same full key as C-Two generated registries, and rejects same id/hash FastDB refs whose version, schema, media type, or capabilities would otherwise register a runtime codec under a key that does not match the method wire spec. It also rejects non-string key fields instead of stringifying them, matching C-Two's descriptor interpretation.
47. Implemented FastDB mutable abstract container bridge ergonomics slice: FastDB automatic bridge derivation treats `MutableMapping` as mapping-shaped and `MutableSequence` as sequence-shaped in the existing feature and batch bridge families, so writable-interface resource annotations stay on the same C-Two codec-neutral bridge path instead of falling through to object-list output or no-bridge behavior.
48. Implemented FastDB fixed tuple return bridge slice: FastDB automatic bridge derivation recursively maps fixed CRM tuple return items through existing scalar, `Array`, single-feature, and `Batch` output converters, so multi-payload CRM returns can adapt existing tuple-shaped resource returns without adding C-Two-side fastdb logic.
49. Implemented FastDB scalar Array bridge guardrail slice: FastDB `coerce_array(...)` and derived `Array[Scalar]` output hooks reject mappings before Python can reinterpret mapping keys as array elements, keeping scalar-array adaptation aligned with batch and column malformed-source guardrails.
49. Implemented FastDB row-tuple bridge ergonomics slice: FastDB automatic bridge derivation maps `Batch[Feature]` inputs into resource row tuples and maps row-tuple batch outputs back into feature batches in schema field order, with derivation-time arity/scalar-item guardrails and runtime non-tuple/wrong-length output guardrails.
50. Implemented FastDB table-like batch output bridge slice: FastDB object-batch output helpers normalize DataFrame/Arrow/Polars-style row-record exports before generic iteration, while preserving existing row-iterable behavior for custom objects with unrelated `to_dict()` helpers.
51. Implemented C-Two TypeScript relay route payload-limit guardrail slice: generated relay-aware HTTP transports now retain resolved route `max_payload_size`, skip candidates too small for the encoded request payload, throw a local 413 when no candidate can carry the payload, validate malformed or non-positive route fields before data-plane calls, and reject resolved routes whose CRM identity does not match the requested contract.
52. Implemented FastDB non-iterable table-like batch output bridge slice: derived `Batch[Feature]` output hooks now accept row-record export objects that are not themselves iterable, and C-Two thread-local, direct IPC, and explicit HTTP relay smokes use the same codec-neutral bridge execution slot.
53. Implemented FastDB input hold ownership guardrail slice: C-Two grid direct IPC smoke now proves fastdb call-db input transferables use view-mode request handling when `from_buffer` materializes values, leaving no active `resource_input` lease after `get_grid_infos`.
54. Implemented raw fastdb feature input hold ownership guardrail slice: raw feature transferables also opt out of C-Two auto input hold when their `from_buffer` hook materializes feature objects rather than returning retained resource-facing views.
55. Implemented FastDB table-object batch input bridge slice: derived `Batch[Feature]` input hooks can now construct resource table objects from row records through `from_records` / `from_pylist` / `from_dicts` factory methods or a one-argument constructor, covering DataFrame-style resource APIs while keeping C-Two fastdb-neutral.
56. Implemented FastDB producer-side table-like batch input slice: call-db `Batch[Feature]` serialization and derived bridge input hooks now normalize table-like row-record exporters before requiring iterable rows, so DataFrame/Arrow/Polars-style client values can enter the same fastdb ABI path across thread-local, direct IPC, and relay.
57. Implemented FastDB producer-side scalar Array iterable slice: call-db `Array[Scalar]` serialization now accepts ordinary non-mapping, non-bytes-like iterables for both columnar and object-graph profiles, rejects scalar string/bytes/memoryview and mapping inputs before Python can reinterpret them, and the C-Two FastDB integration smoke passes tuple array inputs through thread-local, direct IPC, and relay paths.
58. Implemented FastDB scalar Array output iterable guardrail slice: call-db `Array[Scalar]` output serialization now has direct FastDB tests for columnar generators, object-graph generators, and mapping rejection, plus C-Two remote IPC/HTTP smokes proving a tuple-returning resource can be serialized by the fastdb output transferable without C-Two parsing fastdb.
59. Implemented FastDB variadic tuple row-sequence bridge slice: derived `Batch[Feature]` input/output hooks now treat `tuple[Row, ...]` as an immutable row sequence for tuple rows, mapping rows, domain object rows, or fastdb feature rows, while non-variadic tuple annotations still mean tuple columns and scalar variadic tuples fail during derivation.
60. Implemented C-Two TypeScript relay resolve retry guardrail slice: generated relay-aware HTTP transports now have runnable smoke coverage for both thrown resolve transport failures and retryable 5xx resolve responses before they proceed to the data-plane route, keeping route acquisition retry policy in C-Two-generated transport rather than FastDB helpers.
61. Implemented C-Two TypeScript HTTP transport boundary guardrail slice: generated explicit and relay-aware HTTP bytes transports validate options, base/anchor URLs, injected/global `fetch`, and user headers at construction; non-reserved custom headers still pass through, while `Content-Type` and expected-contract headers cannot be overridden.
62. Implemented C-Two TypeScript relay URL authority guardrail slice: generated explicit base URLs, relay-aware anchor URLs, and resolved route `relay_url` values must be absolute HTTP(S) URLs without whitespace, credentials, query, or fragment components before any resolve/data-plane fetch can use them; resolved route URL failures are classified as malformed resolve payload shape, so provider helpers such as FastDB registries cannot inherit malformed relay authority.
63. Implemented FastDB Batch column item annotation guardrail slice: derived `Batch[Feature]` tuple-column, dict/mapping-column, and split-column resource bridges now reject non-scalar or nested column item annotations such as `list[list[int]]` during FastDB-owned derivation before C-Two can register a half-bridge.
64. Implemented C-Two strict FastDB bytes capability guardrail slice: strict TypeScript codegen now requires `org.fastdb.call-db` method wire refs to include the `bytes` capability as well as the correct call-db schema and schema hash, so generated bytes transports cannot accept a FastDB requirement that no bytes-level provider can honestly satisfy.
65. Implemented C-Two TypeScript custom HTTP header syntax guardrail slice: generated explicit and relay-aware HTTP bytes transports now reject custom header names outside HTTP token syntax and custom header values containing CR, LF, or NUL before caller metadata can reach `fetch`.
66. Implemented C-Two TypeScript route contract text guardrail slice: generated explicit and relay-aware HTTP bytes transports now validate caller-supplied CRM namespace/name/version text against the Rust CRM tag boundary, including UTF-8 byte length, surrounding whitespace, control characters, and path/tag separators before building expected-contract headers or relay resolve queries.
67. Implemented C-Two TypeScript custom HTTP header prototype-safety guardrail slice: generated HTTP transports now store normalized caller headers in a null-prototype record so valid token header names such as `__proto__` are preserved as data properties instead of being dropped or interpreted through JavaScript object prototype semantics.
68. Implemented C-Two TypeScript route and method text guardrail slice: generated explicit and relay-aware HTTP bytes transports now validate `routeName` and method text against the Rust route/method boundary, including UTF-8 byte length, surrounding whitespace, control characters, and separator policy while preserving `/` as a valid named-route character.
69. Implemented FastDB scalar bridge resource annotation guardrail slice: derived fastdb scalar input/output bridges now accept untyped or scalar-shaped resource annotations but reject non-scalar resource annotations such as mapping or sequence values during FastDB-owned derivation before C-Two can register a misleading scalar bridge hook.
70. Implemented FastDB TypeScript WASM-owned payload ingress slice: fastdb4ts now exposes `FastdbOwnedBytes` / `allocateFastdbOwnedBytes(...)`, and `loadDatabaseFromBytes(...)` can consume a caller-populated WASM heap buffer through `WxDatabase.loadFromOwnedHeap(...)` without allocating or copying a second JS-to-WASM buffer, giving future C-Two TypeScript transports a zero-copy ingress target while ordinary HTTP `Uint8Array` responses keep the existing single-copy path.
71. Implemented FastDB TypeScript transport-owned payload surface slice: `ORM.fromBuffer(...)`, `FastSerializer.loads(...)`, `decodeFastdbC2Feature(...)`, `decodeFastdbC2CallDb(...)`, and `viewFastdbC2CallDb(...)` now accept `FastdbOwnedBytes`, so provider/runtime entrypoints can consume a transport-filled WASM payload without first coercing it back to an empty or copied `Uint8Array`.
72. Implemented C-Two/FastDB TypeScript provider-owned held response payload guardrail slice: generic generated `C2EncodedClientTransport` may return `C2ResponsePayload` including provider-owned objects with `byteLength`, codec `decode(...)` / `fromBuffer(...)` receive that exact payload, held calls retain the same provider-owned response on `C2HeldResult.buffer`, FastDB generated typed facades accept that widened raw held buffer shape, and built-in explicit/relay-aware HTTP transports at that point remained byte-only `Uint8Array` transports until the follow-up allocator/WASM-ingress integration.
73. Implemented C-Two TypeScript HTTP response payload allocator slice: generated explicit and relay-aware HTTP transports accept a codec-neutral `responsePayloadAllocator`, require `Content-Length` and a readable body stream by default, stream known-length successful data-plane response chunks into the allocator-provided `Uint8Array` view, optionally support bounded `responsePayloadUnknownLengthStrategy: "buffer"` by snapshotting unknown-length stream chunks before allocating and copying into the provider-owned payload, return the allocator's provider-owned payload, release allocations on stream/reader failures, and keep the no-allocator path as ordinary byte-only `Uint8Array`.
74. Implemented C-Two TypeScript HTTP response payload allocator failure guardrail slice: generated allocator-backed HTTP response reads now release the allocated result when `body.getReader()` itself fails, release invalid allocation shapes before stream reads, release provider-owned payloads through the shared allocation release path, reject short streams, overlong streams, and non-`Uint8Array` chunks before returning a malformed provider-owned payload, keep successful allocated responses retained for the caller, and keep the no-allocator HTTP path as ordinary `Uint8Array`.
75. Implemented FastDB generated response allocator adapter slice: FastDB TypeScript helper generation now emits `createFastdbC2ResponsePayloadAllocator(module)`, which returns the structural C-Two allocator shape backed by `allocateFastdbOwnedBytes(...)` for non-empty responses and an empty `Uint8Array` payload for zero-length responses, so generated C-Two relay-aware HTTP transports can stream data-plane response bytes directly into FastDB-owned WASM memory without C-Two importing FastDB.
76. Implemented allocator documentation synchronization slice: C-Two roadmap/vision and FastDB docs now describe `createFastdbC2ResponsePayloadAllocator(module)` as an implemented FastDB generated adapter for C-Two allocator-backed HTTP ingress, rather than a future missing piece, while keeping IPC SHM parity, more efficient unknown-length/chunked HTTP body handling beyond the buffered fallback, broader TypeScript SDK packaging/runtime guidance, and non-native variable-length list layouts as future work.
77. Implemented C-Two TypeScript unknown-length allocator fallback slice: generated explicit and relay-aware HTTP transports now accept `responsePayloadUnknownLengthStrategy: "reject" | "buffer"` plus `responsePayloadUnknownLengthMaxBytes` with a 64 MiB default and 2_147_483_647 hard maximum, default to strict `reject` when `responsePayloadAllocator` is configured and `Content-Length` is absent, and opt into a bounded buffered fallback that reads unknown-length response chunks, snapshots each chunk, rejects over-limit bodies before allocating, allocates the exact final byte length, copies into the allocator-owned view, and returns the provider-owned payload without falling back to `arrayBuffer()`.
78. Implemented C-Two TypeScript provider-owned response release guardrail slice: generated codec transports now best-effort release provider-owned response payloads when output codec lookup, `decode(...)`, or `fromBuffer(...)` fails after a wire response has been received, and held decode-fallback results release their retained raw provider-owned buffer on `HeldResult.release()` without closing the materialized decoded value.
79. Implemented FastDB table-like tuple-row batch output bridge slice: derived `Batch[Feature]` tuple-row output hooks now normalize table-like producers that expose `to_pylist()`, `to_dicts()`, or `to_dict('records')` before tuple-row validation, so non-iterable table wrappers compose with tuple-row resource returns while malformed table-like column mappings fail at the bridge boundary instead of iterating mapping keys; C-Two integration coverage now drives the same shape through thread-local, direct IPC, and explicit HTTP relay via the sibling FastDB provider.
80. Implemented C-Two TypeScript HTTP response Content-Length hard-cap guardrail slice: generated explicit and relay-aware HTTP transports now reject response `Content-Length` values greater than `2_147_483_647` before calling a provider allocator, reading a success body stream, or materializing no-allocator/CRM-error `arrayBuffer()` bodies, and the same constant bounds unknown-length buffered allocator fallback configuration.
81. Implemented C-Two TypeScript HTTP response Content-Length match guardrail slice: generated explicit and relay-aware HTTP transports now validate that no-allocator success responses and 500 CRM-error binary bodies with declared `Content-Length` materialize to the same byte length, matching the allocator stream path's existing short/overlong body checks.
82. Implemented C-Two TypeScript HTTP text response Content-Length hard-cap guardrail slice: generated explicit and relay-aware HTTP transports now validate declared `Content-Length` before reading non-500 data-plane error text bodies and relay resolve text bodies, including both non-200 resolve errors and 200 resolve JSON responses.
83. Implemented FastDB Iterator abstract container bridge ergonomics slice: FastDB automatic bridge derivation now treats `Iterator[...]` and `typing.Iterator[...]` as sequence-shaped resource annotations where the existing bridge already materializes rows or columns, returns real iterator objects for resource input annotations that ask for iterators, consumes iterator resource outputs for scalar `Array`, tuple-row `Batch`, mapping-row `Batch`, tuple-column `Batch`, and mapping-column `Batch` conversions, and C-Two integration coverage drives an iterator-shaped `cc.register(..., bridge=...)` resource across thread-local, direct IPC, and explicit HTTP relay without adding C-Two-side fastdb logic.
84. Implemented FastDB TypeScript input sequence parity slice: fastdb4ts C-Two call-db runtime now accepts sequence-like input values for `Array[Scalar]` and `Batch[Feature]` tables where TypeScript users naturally pass typed arrays, indexed array-like objects, sets, or generators, rejects ambiguous strings, `ArrayBuffer`/`DataView`, `Map`, functions, and non-indexed array-like values before they can be interpreted as item streams, and checks columnar fast-path eligibility from metadata before consuming one-shot iterables so unsupported fast paths fall back without draining generators.
85. Implemented C-Two TypeScript direct IPC transport and response allocator ingress slice: generated `createIpcEncodedTransport(...)` maps explicit `ipc://` addresses to Rust-compatible socket paths, performs the v2 IPC handshake through an injected connection, validates advertised route CRM identity, method table, and `max_payload_size` before sending a call frame, sends `FLAG_CALL_V2` requests, decodes inline `FLAG_REPLY_V2` success, CRM-error, and route-not-found replies, assembles chunked success replies, rejects SHM replies as unsupported by this generated transport, and can copy successful inline or chunked replies into the same codec-neutral `responsePayloadAllocator` shape used by HTTP transports without importing FastDB.
86. Implemented C-Two TypeScript IPC SHM response reader seam: generated `createIpcEncodedTransport(...)` now preserves server handshake SHM prefix/segment metadata, decodes buddy reply payloads, sends success replies through optional `responseShmReader.read(block, destination?)` and `responseShmReader.release(block)` hooks, supports allocator-backed SHM reads into provider-owned views, preserves CRM-error and route-not-found semantics on buddy frames, rejects chunked SHM replies for now, and validates missing readers, truncated buddy payloads, invalid buddy flags, empty or oversized SHM data sizes, invalid allocator outputs, and advertised buddy segment ranges before handing metadata to reader code.
87. Implemented C-Two TypeScript IPC SHM reader release contract: generated IPC transports now require `responseShmReader` to be an object with `read(...)` and `release(...)`, copy no-allocator SHM reads into an owned destination before releasing the block so returned payloads cannot alias a released runtime mapping, release SHM blocks after successful reads and after post-read byte-length validation failures, and release allocator-owned response payloads if SHM release fails after allocation.
88. Implemented C-Two TypeScript IPC chunked request transport: generated `createIpcEncodedTransport(...)` exposes `requestChunkSize`, keeps small requests inline, sends larger requests as Rust-compatible chunked request frames, requires server `CAP_CHUNKED`, rejects invalid chunk sizing and unrepresentable chunk counts before writing, and closes the connection after partial chunked request write failure.
89. Implemented C-Two TypeScript IPC request SHM writer transport: generated `createIpcEncodedTransport(...)` now accepts a structural `requestShmWriter` and `requestShmThreshold`, advertises writer prefix/segments in the client handshake, sends large request payloads as Rust-compatible `FLAG_CALL_V2 | FLAG_BUDDY` frames with `[buddy_payload][call_control]`, validates writer block metadata against the advertised handshake segments, releases invalid or unsent request blocks locally, releases dedicated request blocks after server response, and leaves non-dedicated buddy blocks to the Rust server's cross-process free authority after successful server consumption.
90. Implemented C-Two TypeScript Node/POSIX dedicated SHM helper slice: generated TypeScript now exports structural `C2NodePosixShmFileSystem` / `C2NodePosixShmFileHandle` contracts plus `createNodePosixDedicatedResponseShmReader(...)` and `createNodePosixDedicatedRequestShmWriter(...)`, maps POSIX SHM names into a configurable SHM directory, reads dedicated response payload bytes after the 64-byte c2-mem dedicated header, marks `read_done=1` on response release, writes dedicated request payloads into page-aligned header-plus-payload files, advertises no buddy segments, returns dedicated buddy metadata, and unlinks dedicated request segments on writer release.
91. Later: close remaining TypeScript SDK transport parity gaps beyond the completed HTTP relay-aware helper, generated held/fromBuffer path, route payload-limit guardrail, FastDB typed facade, call/resolve timeout guardrails, route cache TTL guardrail, resolve retry guardrails, route contract/path text guardrails, custom header syntax/prototype-safety guardrails, provider-owned held response payload retention, response payload allocator streaming ingress, allocator failure guardrails, FastDB allocator adapter, HTTP transport boundary guardrails, allocator documentation synchronization, bounded unknown-length buffered fallback, provider-owned response failure-release guardrails, HTTP response Content-Length hard-cap guardrail, HTTP response Content-Length match guardrail, HTTP text response Content-Length hard-cap guardrail, FastDB TypeScript input sequence parity, generated direct IPC inline/chunked transport plus response allocator ingress, generated IPC SHM response reader seam, generated IPC SHM reader release contract, generated IPC chunked request transport, generated IPC request SHM writer transport, generated dedicated-only Node/POSIX SHM helpers, and generated native-buddy wrapper contracts; ship broader real IPC coverage and publishable SDK packaging beyond the initial Node/POSIX `c2-mem-ffi` direct IPC smoke plus Bun/Deno or equivalent bindings over the same Rust-owned substrates; broaden TypeScript columnar field runtime coverage for non-native variable-length list layouts; keep expanding bridge derivation coverage where real resource shapes expose gaps; and add lower-level fixed-table or heap-backed column writes only when measurements prove they beat mutable bulk append.

## Phase 26: Object-Graph Call-DB Scalar And Array TypeScript Runtime

- [x] Implemented materialized TypeScript encode/decode for object-graph call-db scalar and scalar-array tables by mapping schema-visible call-db table names to dynamic ObjectEngine layers.
- [x] Preserved object-graph feature-table behavior and feature dependency graph identity while allowing scalar, array, and feature tables to share one `fastdb.call.object-graph.v1` payload.
- [x] Added runtime and codegen guardrails that reject layer-name collisions between dynamic scalar/array table names and feature or dependency class names before payload construction or helper generation.
- [x] Added Python planner guardrails for the same object-graph layer-name collisions, preserved empty object-graph array/batch layers, and added malformed call-db table-name/cardinality descriptor guardrails in fastdb TypeScript helper generation and runtime.
- [x] Added an explicit-close object-graph call-db view surface over a retained `WxDatabase` load context; it supports materialized row/scalar/array/feature access and keeps column access columnar-only.

## Acceptance Evidence

Each implementation slice must finish with a review that proves the invariants above through source-to-sink evidence, not only happy-path tests. At minimum, the final slice needs focused fastdb planner tests, C-Two descriptor/export/codegen tests, thread-local/direct IPC/relay grid smoke, held-view lease tests, import scans that prove C-Two core does not import fastdb, and negative tests for Python-only fallback diagnostics.

## Phase 4 Review Evidence

- Closed-loop review froze these invariants for the initial grid smoke: grid portable wire refs must be `org.fastdb.call-db` or no-payload refs with no pickle, bridge conversion must run for thread-local/direct IPC/explicit HTTP relay, direct IPC hold must expose a retained `FastdbCallView`, C-Two core/SDK/CLI production code must not import fastdb, and docs must not describe completed bridge/grid smoke work as missing.
- Source-to-sink evidence now covers `examples/python/grid/grid_fdb_crm.py` as the CRM producer, `fastdb4py.c_two_provider.CTwoFastdbCodecProvider` and `fastdb4py.c_two_call.FastdbCallPlan` as provider/schema producers, `sdk/python/src/c_two/transport/registry.py` and `sdk/python/src/c_two/transport/server/native.py` as bridge registration/storage, `sdk/python/src/c_two/transport/client/proxy.py` and native dispatch as thread-local/direct IPC/HTTP consumers, and `sdk/python/tests/integration/test_grid_fastdb_bridge_smoke.py` as the end-to-end guardrail.
- Review finding remediated: `examples/python/grid/fastdb_bridge.py` previously used `zip(levels, global_ids)` for `get_active_grid_infos` output and would silently truncate mismatched arrays; it now raises `ValueError`, and `test_grid_fastdb_bridge_rejects_mismatched_active_output_lengths` guards the behavior.
- Review finding remediated: grid tests previously checked only the development descriptor; `test_grid_fastdb_contract_uses_call_db_refs` now also calls `cc.export_contract_descriptor(GridFastdb)` so the same grid CRM passes `c-two.contract.v1` portable export and native validation with no `python-pickle-default`.
- Review finding remediated: roadmap/vision/plan text in both repos still called the C-Two bridge, fastdb `Array`/`Batch`, and grid smoke future gaps; those docs now distinguish completed initial slices from then-remaining work such as object-graph call-db, scalar/nullable policy guardrails, Arrow-grid migration, bridge derivation, and TypeScript/WASM runtime.
- Verification run after remediation: `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_grid_fastdb_bridge_smoke.py -q --timeout=30` passed with 6 tests; `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_registry.py::TestRegisterConnect::test_register_accepts_bridged_resource_annotation_mismatch sdk/python/tests/integration/test_registry.py::TestRegisterConnect::test_direct_ipc_calls_apply_resource_bridge sdk/python/tests/integration/test_registry.py::TestRegisterConnect::test_explicit_http_relay_calls_apply_resource_bridge -q --timeout=30` passed with 3 tests; `uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/unit/test_codec_provider.py sdk/python/tests/unit/test_contract_export.py sdk/python/tests/unit/test_resource_conformance.py -q --timeout=30` passed with 26 tests; `python -m compileall -q examples/python/grid/grid_fdb_crm.py examples/python/grid/fastdb_bridge.py sdk/python/tests/integration/test_grid_fastdb_bridge_smoke.py` passed; `rg -n "import fastdb|from fastdb|fastdb4py" core sdk/python/src/c_two cli -g '!*.md'` returned no matches; `git diff --check` passed.

## Phase 5 Review Evidence

- The initial fastdb bridge helper slice added `fastdb4py.c_two_bridge` with dependency-neutral conversion helpers only; it imports fastdb schema/registry utilities but does not import C-Two, and C-Two production code still has no fastdb imports.
- The initial C-Two grid bridge slice used `coerce_scalar(...)`, `coerce_array(...)`, `object_batch_mapper(...)`, and `batch_from_columns(...)` to keep resource conversion explicit while removing repeated per-field construction code; later automatic derivation replaced the hand-written grid bridge with `derive_c_two_bridge(...)`.
- Review finding remediated: bridge helpers previously accepted unknown `field_map`, `converters`, `defaults`, or `columns` keys and would silently ignore typos; they now fail fast, and tests cover unknown columns, unknown converters, unknown field maps, and non-callable converters.
- Verification run after implementation and remediation: `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_bridge.py tests/python/test_c_two_call_db.py tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py tests/python/test_c_two_schema_provider.py -q` passed with 56 tests in the fastdb repo; `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_grid_fastdb_bridge_smoke.py -q --timeout=30` passed with 6 tests in the C-Two repo; `python -m compileall -q /Users/soku/Desktop/codespace/WorldInProgress/fastdb/python/fastdb4py/c_two_bridge.py /Users/soku/Desktop/codespace/WorldInProgress/fastdb/tests/python/test_c_two_bridge.py examples/python/grid/fastdb_bridge.py` passed.

## Phase 6 Review Evidence

- The object-graph call-db slice makes fastdb, not C-Two, select `fastdb.call.object-graph.v1` when method payload feature schemas contain `ref` or `list[ref]`; C-Two still only sees an opaque `org.fastdb.call-db` `CodecRef`.
- Review finding remediated: the first object-graph implementation hashed only the root feature table, so a dependency feature schema change could leave the method codec identity unchanged; call-db feature table descriptors now include `feature_schema_dependencies` with dependency feature schema hashes, and TypeScript helper generation validates those sidecar schemas.
- Review finding remediated: object-graph call-db cannot currently expose a true retained columnar view, so its `CodecRef` capabilities are `["bytes"]`; provider `from_buffer` materializes object-graph output rather than returning `FastdbCallView`, while columnar call-db still returns retained views.
- Verification run after implementation and remediation: `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_bridge.py tests/python/test_c_two_call_db.py tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py tests/python/test_c_two_schema_provider.py -q` passed with 60 tests in the fastdb repo; `python -m compileall -q python/fastdb4py/c_two_call.py python/fastdb4py/c_two_provider.py python/fastdb4py/codegen/c_two_ts.py tests/python/test_c_two_call_db.py tests/python/test_c_two_schema_provider.py tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py` passed; `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_grid_fastdb_bridge_smoke.py -q --timeout=30` passed with 6 tests in the C-Two repo.

## Phase 7 Review Evidence

- The scalar/nullable strictness slice makes fastdb call-db claim only explicit fastdb scalar aliases such as `I32`, `F64`, `STR`, and `BOOL`; Python builtin `int`, `float`, `str`, and `bool` now fail planning inside fastdb and let C-Two use Python-only pickle fallback paths, while `T | None` / `Optional[T]` call-db annotations are rejected until fastdb has a real null ABI.
- Review finding remediated: before this slice, installing the fastdb provider could promote a prototype CRM method like `def increment(amount: int) -> int` into `org.fastdb.call-db`, and nullable fastdb aliases failed with generic annotation errors rather than an ABI policy decision; `sdk/python/tests/integration/test_fastdb_codec_provider_smoke.py::test_fastdb_provider_does_not_claim_python_builtin_scalar_methods` and `::test_fastdb_provider_does_not_claim_python_nullable_builtin_methods` now prove Python builtin scalar methods stay on `python-pickle-default`, while fastdb planner/provider tests prove nullable call-db annotations are refused.
- Verification run after implementation and nullable remediation: `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_bridge.py tests/python/test_c_two_call_db.py tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py tests/python/test_c_two_schema_provider.py -q` passed with 64 tests in the fastdb repo; `python -m compileall -q python/fastdb4py/c_two_call.py tests/python/test_c_two_call_db.py tests/python/test_c_two_schema_provider.py tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py` passed; `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_fastdb_codec_provider_smoke.py sdk/python/tests/integration/test_grid_fastdb_bridge_smoke.py -q --timeout=30` passed with 10 tests in the C-Two repo; `git diff --check` passed in both repos.

## Phase 8 Review Evidence

- The structured diagnostics slice adds a provider-neutral `method_codec_diagnostics(...)` query in C-Two while keeping runtime `resolve_method_codec(...)` behavior unchanged; providers that only expose diagnostics are skipped by annotation-level codec resolution and cannot break CRM decoration.
- FastDB's optional C-Two wrapper now reports `fastdb_call_db_not_planned` diagnostics that carry the method, input/output position, and planner reason, such as Python builtin scalar fallback or nullable call-db rejection.
- Review finding remediated: the first diagnostics-only provider implementation was accepted by `cc.use_codec(...)` but annotation-level `resolve_codec(...)` still attempted to call the provider object when it lacked `candidates_for_type`; `sdk/python/src/c_two/crm/codec.py` now skips non-callable providers without type candidates, and `test_contract_descriptor_diagnostics_include_provider_method_reasons` guards this path.

## Phase 9 Review Evidence

- The list-ABI cleanup slice removes CRM-level `list[Feature]` from fastdb call-db planning and keeps `Batch[Feature]` as the only portable feature batch spelling; this does not affect `list[ref]` fields inside fastdb feature schemas.
- Review finding remediated: previous tests and docs still used `list[Feature]` as a compatibility path, which could make it a de facto portable ABI; FastDB planner/codegen/provider tests now use `Batch[Feature]`, and new negative tests prove `list[Feature]` and `list[Scalar]` are rejected with `Batch[Feature]` / `Array[Scalar]` guidance.
- C-Two integration guardrail: `test_fastdb_provider_diagnoses_list_feature_crm_spelling` installs the real fastdb provider and proves `cc.contract_descriptor_diagnostics(...)` reports `fastdb_call_db_not_planned` with `Batch[Feature]` guidance for a CRM method annotated with `list[Point]`.

## Phase 11 Review Evidence

- The automatic bridge derivation slice keeps the final per-method bridge plan in C-Two while moving schema-aware derivation to fastdb: `fastdb4py.c_two_bridge.derive_bridge_hooks(...)` inspects CRM/resource annotations, and `derive_c_two_bridge(cc, CRM, Resource)` calls the passed `cc.bridge(...)` factory without importing C-Two inside fastdb.
- Closed-loop invariants reviewed: C-Two production remains fastdb-neutral; bridge conversion must still execute through `cc.register(..., bridge=...)`; automatic derivation must not silently widen unsupported tuple-column shapes; scalar alias conversion must cover the public fastdb string/bytes aliases; and grid thread-local/direct IPC/relay/hold tests must still exercise the derived bridge rather than the old hand-written functions.
- Review finding remediated: automatic derivation originally looked up resource methods on the resource type, so instance-level callables could be skipped; it now resolves methods on the supplied resource object or class, with `test_derive_bridge_hooks_supports_instance_level_methods` as the guardrail.
- Review finding remediated: tuple-to-`Batch[Feature]` derivation originally checked only tuple length and could fail later with a generic non-iterable column error; it now rejects non-`list[...]` tuple columns during derivation, with `test_derive_bridge_hooks_rejects_non_list_tuple_columns` as the guardrail.
- Review finding remediated: automatic scalar conversion originally omitted `WSTR` and `BYTES`; it now maps `WSTR` through `str` and `BYTES` through `bytes`, with `test_derive_bridge_hooks_maps_wstr_and_bytes_aliases` as the guardrail.
- Verification run after implementation and remediation: `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_bridge.py -q` passed with 16 tests in the fastdb repo; `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_grid_fastdb_bridge_smoke.py -q --timeout=30` passed with 6 tests in the C-Two repo.

## Phase 12 Review Evidence

- The TypeScript runtime helper slice keeps C-Two fastdb-neutral and changes only fastdb-owned schemas/codegen/runtime: fastdb call-db descriptors now include `value_position` metadata for scalar fields and array/feature tables so generated TypeScript bindings can reconstruct method argument and return order without guessing from object property order.
- Generated fastdb TypeScript helper bindings now call fastdb4ts runtime helpers instead of throwing placeholder errors. The runtime supports generated columnar feature encode/decode, generated columnar call-db encode/decode for scalar tables, array tables, feature tables, single/many cardinalities, and empty output tables, generated object-graph feature and scalar/array/feature-table object-graph call-db encode/decode, plus explicit-close object-graph row/scalar/array/feature views.
- Review finding remediated: the first generated binding interface did not structurally match the fastdb4ts runtime interface because it omitted the feature constructor shape required by runtime table materialization; generated interfaces now require constructors with `name` and `schema`, and a generated helper `tsc --noEmit` smoke guards the contract.
- Review finding remediated: the first encode runtime left temporary ORMs open on error paths; runtime encoders now close temporary ORM handles in `finally`, while decoders intentionally keep ORM handles alive because returned mapped rows depend on the underlying WASM database handle.
- Review finding remediated: fastdb schema export collapsed `BOOL` to `u8`, which made generated TypeScript helper types say `number` for boolean fields and would affect grid's `activate` / `deleted` fields; `BOOL` now exports as `bool`, call-db boolean scalar/array round-trips return booleans, and fastdb4ts has a boolean call-db runtime test.
- Review finding remediated: TypeScript helper generation could emit callable columnar bindings for `bytes` and `list` fields even though the current fastdb4ts ORM encoder cannot write those field kinds; codegen now rejects those schemas with deterministic diagnostics until matching runtime support exists.
- Review finding remediated: exported fastdb4ts runtime helpers originally trusted hand-constructed binding objects once the profile string matched; they now validate `codecId` before encode/decode so a feature codec ref cannot be routed through the call-db runtime or vice versa.
- Verification run after implementation and remediation: `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_bridge.py tests/python/test_c_two_call_db.py tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py tests/python/test_c_two_schema_provider.py -q` passed with 76 tests in the fastdb repo; `npm --prefix ts/fastdb4ts run test:ts` passed with 32 TypeScript runtime tests; a generated helper project compiled with `tsc --noEmit`; `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/unit/test_contract_export.py sdk/python/tests/unit/test_codec_provider.py sdk/python/tests/integration/test_fastdb_codec_provider_smoke.py sdk/python/tests/integration/test_grid_fastdb_bridge_smoke.py -q --timeout=30` passed with 26 tests in the C-Two repo; the C-Two production import scan returned no fastdb imports; compileall and `git diff --check` passed in both repos.

## Phase 13 Review Evidence

- The held column-view slice keeps C-Two production fastdb-neutral and changes only fastdb's Python retained-view facade plus the grid integration guardrail; the call-db wire format, `CodecRef`, schema text, and schema hash are unchanged because only the consumer-side access pattern changed.
- Closed-loop invariant: a columnar `fdb.Batch[T]` output consumed through `cc.hold(...)` must allow high-performance callers to remain on the retained response buffer and use fastdb's column accessor, while the lifetime remains owned by C-Two `HeldResult.release()`.
- Guardrails added: fastdb's `test_call_db_table_view_exposes_column_accessor_without_copy` fails if column access materializes the response buffer through `bytes(...)`, fastdb's column-view release test fails if `columns.level` can bypass the retained-buffer lifetime check, and C-Two's direct IPC grid hold smoke now asserts `held.value.table('return_0').column.level` and `.global_id`.

## Phase 14 Review Evidence

- The TypeScript encode/codegen smoke slice keeps C-Two production fastdb-neutral: C-Two exports `c-two.contract.v1` with opaque `org.fastdb.call-db` refs, while fastdb owns the sidecar `fastdb.call-db.schema.v1` descriptors, TypeScript helper generation, and fastdb4ts runtime encode/decode.

The implementation was replaced with a mutable bulk append path that avoids `ORM.push(...)`; FastDB now has a generated grid-like TypeScript helper smoke that compiles generated TS, executes it under Node, and fails if the generated helper runtime falls back to `ORM.push(...)`.
