## Phase 15 Review Evidence

- The Python-only fallback clean-cut slice freezes this invariant: if a CRM method payload is not claimed by fastdb or another explicit portable provider, C-Two may still run it for Python prototypes through default pickle transferables, but the descriptor must identify it as `python-pickle-default`, diagnostics must say `python_only_pickle`, portable export must reject it, and TypeScript codegen must never treat it as an implicit built-in runtime codec.
- Source-to-sink review evidence: `sdk/python/src/c_two/crm/transferable.py` now asks method-level providers and annotation providers before falling directly to `create_default_transferable(...)`; `sdk/python/src/c_two/crm/descriptor.py` turns default transferables into `python-pickle-default`, rejects that wire ref in portable mode, and reports `python_only_pickle`; `core/foundation/c2-codegen/src/lib.rs` now emits codec requirements for every non-null codec ref and strict mode allows only fastdb refs; `core/foundation/c2-contract/src/lib.rs` already rejects `python-pickle-default` in portable descriptors.
- Review finding remediated: the old automatic portable control-codec transferable path could make Python-native `int`, `list[int]`, and tuple/list return shapes look portable even though the current fastdb-first policy says they are Python-only prototype paths. The implementation removes that automatic provider path, updates Arrow/grid/infer tests to expect pickle fallback for native control parameters, and updates Rust codegen tests so non-fastdb primitive wire codecs are opaque requirements rather than hidden built-ins.
- Guardrails added: `test_export_contract_descriptor_rejects_python_native_primitives_as_nonportable`, `test_contract_descriptor_diagnostics_report_python_only_and_non_fastdb_paths`, fastdb provider scalar/nullable smoke tests, Arrow/grid/infer tests, and Rust codegen tests together prove Python-native paths are nonportable, provider non-claims stay visible, and non-fastdb codecs require explicit runtime stubs.

## Phase 16 Review Evidence

Later runtime slices now satisfy that invariant for object-graph feature payloads and scalar/array/feature-table object-graph call-db payloads.

The broad rejection has now been replaced by ObjectEngine-compatible WASM runtime helpers, generated bindings for object-graph features and scalar/array/feature-table object-graph call-db, and explicit-close object-graph row/scalar/array/feature views.

## Phase 17 Review Evidence

- The fastdb-native bridge no-op slice freezes this invariant: if a resource method already accepts and returns the exact same fastdb ABI annotations as the CRM method, automatic bridge derivation must not add input/output hooks that copy scalars, arrays, or batches.
- Review finding remediated: `derive_bridge_hooks(...)` previously treated fastdb-native resource methods as if they needed domain-resource adaptation, so `fdb.I32`, `fdb.Array[...]`, and `fdb.Batch[...]` paths could be wrapped and materialized unnecessarily. FastDB now detects exact fastdb ABI annotation equivalence and skips those methods, while still deriving hooks for the existing grid/domain-resource pattern.
- Guardrails added: `test_derive_bridge_hooks_skips_fastdb_native_resource_methods` locks the no-op path, while the existing bridge tests and C-Two grid smoke continue to prove domain resources still receive scalar/array input conversion and object-list or tuple-column `Batch` output conversion.

## Phase 17A Review Evidence

- The batch-input bridge derivation slice freezes this invariant: a fastdb-shaped CRM method with a `Batch[Feature]` input may feed an existing resource method that expects one tuple of same-length Python list columns, but C-Two still stores only a codec-neutral `cc.bridge(...)` plan and never imports fastdb in production code.

FastDB now derives the input hook by reading feature fields in schema order and building `tuple(list per field)`.

- C-Two integration guardrails added: `test_fastdb_derived_bridge_maps_batch_input_to_tuple_columns_thread_local_and_direct_ipc` and `test_fastdb_derived_bridge_maps_batch_input_to_tuple_columns_explicit_http_relay` prove the same derived bridge path applies in thread-local, direct IPC, and explicit HTTP relay execution.

## Phase 17C Review Evidence

- The batch-dict input bridge derivation slice freezes this invariant: a fastdb-shaped CRM method with a `Batch[Feature]` input may feed an existing resource method that explicitly asks for `list[dict[...]]`, but C-Two still stores only a codec-neutral `cc.bridge(...)` plan and never imports fastdb in production code.

FastDB now derives a dict-list input hook only when the list item annotation is `dict` / `dict[...]`, reads feature fields in fastdb schema order, applies existing scalar converters, rejects single mapping values as malformed batches, and reports missing fields before resource code runs.

## Phase 18 Review Evidence

- The grid codegen composition slice freezes this invariant: the real `examples/python/grid/grid_fdb_crm.py` portable descriptor must be enough for fastdb-owned TypeScript helper generation to compile and run against fastdb4ts without C-Two parsing fastdb schemas.
- Guardrail added: `test_grid_fastdb_export_feeds_fastdb_typescript_codegen` now validates the exported grid `schema_sha256` values against fresh fastdb sidecar planning, generates helpers from the real descriptor, builds fastdb4ts, compiles a temporary TypeScript project with `tsc`, runs it under Node, exercises input/output encode/decode plus retained view column access, and monkeypatches `ORM.push(...)` so numeric/boolean call-db helpers cannot silently fall back to row-object encoding.

## Phase 19 Review Evidence

- The TypeScript view slice freezes this invariant: generated fastdb call-db helpers may expose column reads only when the profile is `fastdb.call.columnar.v1`; object-graph call-db views may expose retained database lifetime, `materialize()`, scalar, array, feature, and table row access, but not direct column access or true external-buffer zero-copy.
- Source-to-sink review evidence: C-Two still emits opaque `org.fastdb.call-db` refs and fastdb sidecar descriptors; `python/fastdb4py/codegen/c_two_ts.py` emits generated binding `.view(payload)` and `.scalar(payload, nameOrIndex)` for matching call-db refs; `ts/fastdb4ts/src/c-two.ts` owns `viewFastdbC2CallDb(...)`, `FastdbC2CallDbView`, scalar/single-feature/table/array/column wrappers, `.close()`, and object-graph row/scalar/array/feature access while keeping direct column access columnar-only; ordinary TypeScript decode returns owning feature copies and closes temporary ORMs, so only explicit view objects retain mapped row lifetime; Python `FastdbCallView.scalar(...)` and `FastdbCallView.feature(...)` give matching held-call ergonomics for scalar and cardinality-one feature outputs; tests cover runtime use, generated helper output, generated grid-like compile/run, owning decode, scalar view, single-feature view, object-graph view, and use-after-close guards.
- Boundary note: this is a columnar read-surface and lifetime improvement, not a claim of true external-buffer zero-copy in TypeScript. The current fastdb4ts path now imports the incoming `Uint8Array` into WASM once through owned heap transfer before table/column views are exposed; removing that remaining copy requires lower-level fastdb4ts/WASM or transport support that writes directly into WASM memory.
- Verification run after implementation, review, and remediation: `npm --prefix ts/fastdb4ts run test:ts -- tests/ts/test_c_two_runtime.mjs` passed with 40 TypeScript tests; `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py::test_c_two_typescript_helpers_generate_single_bytes_columnar_feature_runtime tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py::test_c_two_typescript_helpers_reject_columnar_feature_runtime_gaps tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py::test_c_two_typescript_helpers_reject_multiple_bytes_columnar_runtime_gap -q` passed with 3 tests; `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_bridge.py tests/python/test_c_two_call_db.py tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py tests/python/test_c_two_schema_provider.py -q` passed with 92 tests; `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_grid_fastdb_bridge_smoke.py -q --timeout=30` passed with 7 tests; stale TS-view wording scans, C-Two production fastdb-import scan, and `git diff --check` passed in both repos.

## Phase 20 Review Evidence

- The TypeScript columnar schema guardrail slice freezes this invariant: generated helpers and hand-built fastdb4ts C-Two runtime bindings must reject unsupported columnar field metadata at the encode/decode/view boundary, not later through `ORM.push(...)`, `fieldTypeForKind(...)`, arbitrary payload parsing, or mapped-field access. After the numeric-list runtime slice, unsupported list metadata means `list[ref]`, non-native variable-length list items such as string/bytes lists, and hand-built call-db array tables that claim `item.kind = "list"`; native numeric scalar lists are supported.
- Source-to-sink review evidence: C-Two still exports only opaque fastdb codec refs; Python fastdb TypeScript codegen now allows native numeric scalar list fields and rejects only unsupported list item kinds; `ts/embind/fastdb4ts.cpp` exposes list field writes plus list/ref reads; `ts/fastdb4ts/src/orm.ts`, `feature.ts`, `table.ts`, and `c-two.ts` now encode numeric scalar list fields, return owning list arrays for materialized reads, reject list columns as strided columns, and validate hand-built call-db metadata before payload serialization, payload deserialization, or retained-view construction. Feature-class schema validation can use fastdb4ts's schema cache, but call-db binding metadata is revalidated on each call because hand-built JavaScript binding objects are mutable.
- Guardrails added: `test_c_two_runtime.mjs` now covers direct columnar feature bindings with `listOf(I32)`, call-db feature tables carrying numeric list fields through owning decode and retained row reads, rejection of strided column access for list fields, a hand-built array table with `item.kind = "list"`, and a mutable hand-built binding that is valid for the first call then mutated to unsupported list metadata.
- Verification run after numeric-list/object-graph remediation: `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py -q` passed with 26 tests in FastDB; `node --test tests/ts/test_c_two_runtime.mjs` passed with 20 TypeScript tests; `npm --prefix ts/fastdb4ts run test:ts` passed with 46 TypeScript tests. Broader Python/C-Two regression evidence is refreshed in the integration verification section below after the final review loop.

- Phase 48 TypeScript held-call codegen review added a source-to-sink path from generated CRM client methods to provider-owned retained views. C-Two generated clients call `requireHeldTransport(...).hold(...)`; generated codec transports encode the method input exactly like normal calls, call the same bytes transport, then use `codec.fromBuffer(...)` when the output codec supplies it and wrap the result in `C2HeldResult`. `C2HeldResult.release()` is idempotent, releases provider views by calling `release()` or `close()` only when the value came from `fromBuffer(...)`, and is a no-op for `decode(...)` fallback values, so FastDB `FastdbC2CallDbView` lifetime is controlled by the C-Two generated held API while ordinary generated methods still materialize through `decode(...)`. Review found and remediated one provider-side guardrail gap: FastDB generated registries no longer expose a `fromBuffer(...)` method for bindings that only have `decode(...)`, preventing decode-only feature bindings from being released as if they were retained views.

FastDB bridge tests passed with 107 tests, FastDB focused provider/bridge/codegen/schema tests passed with 236 tests, and C-Two FastDB/grid integration passed with 41 tests.
- Phase 74 FastDB input hold ownership guardrail review found that the production defense already existed: FastDB marks input-direction call-db transferables with `_c2_auto_input_hold = False`, and C-Two auto-transfer respects that flag before selecting hold mode. The missing piece was a real C-Two grid/direct IPC source-to-sink guardrail proving request buffers are released for materialized input plans.
- Phase 74 verification after closed-loop remediation: C-Two grid direct IPC now checks `GridFastdb.get_grid_infos._input_buffer_mode == "view"`, verifies the input transferable disables auto input hold, performs a real call, and asserts no active `resource_input` lease remains. The focused FastDB provider test and focused C-Two grid direct IPC/hold tests passed.
- Phase 75 raw feature input hold ownership guardrail review closed the same ownership rule on FastDB's raw feature provider public surface: `FastdbCodecAdapter.from_buffer(...)` materializes feature objects, so generated raw feature transferables must not make C-Two auto-select input hold. This is not the preferred portable CRM method path, but it prevents a public provider bypass.

FastDB now derives an input hook for domain table objects with `from_records`, `from_pylist`, `from_dicts`, or a one-argument constructor, ignores unbound instance factory methods, and rejects constructors with extra required arguments before C-Two registration can accept a half-bridge.

FastDB now normalizes `to_pylist()`, `to_dicts()`, and `to_dict("records")` row-record exporters before batch row validation in both call-db serialization and derived input hooks, including an object-graph `Batch[Feature]` input case with ref fields, while C-Two continues to see only opaque fastdb call-db bytes or codec-neutral bridge hooks.

This keeps application-supplied registries from upgrading a decode-only codec into a held-view codec by function presence alone.

- Phase 98 FastDB BOOL producer truthiness guardrail closed a cross-language data-correctness bypass: Python call-db, Python bridge conversion, fastdb4ts columnar call-db, and fastdb4ts object-graph call-db no longer use Python/JavaScript truthiness for `BOOL` producer values. They parse bools, `0`/`1`, and true/false strings explicitly, and reject ambiguous strings before writing payload bytes.

- Phase 99 FastDB provider installation idempotence closed a real multi-module import and fixture-reset bypass: repeated `install_c_two_provider(cc_module=cc)` calls now reuse the provider cached on the C-Two module/object, re-register that same object through `cc.use_codec(...)` when the codec registry was cleared, reject attempts to replace an already-installed FastDB provider with a different provider instance, and roll back the cached module attribute if first-time `cc.use_codec(...)` registration fails. This prevents one CRM method input/output from resolving multiple identical `org.fastdb.call-db` candidates after repeated imports while avoiding a half-installed provider cache after registration failure.
- Phase 99 verification after closed-loop review: red FastDB unit coverage reproduced a half-installed provider cache when first-time `cc.use_codec(...)` registration failed; after remediation, FastDB schema/provider tests passed with 29 tests, FastDB import-boundary/bridge/call-db/codegen/schema focused tests passed with 285 tests, FastDB Python tests excluding the free-threading stress file passed with 576 tests, and `test_free_threading.py` passed separately with 12 tests. - Phase 100 C-Two TypeScript contract-scoped cache invalidation closed a relay-aware transport performance and routing-scope regression: generated resolve cache keys already included route name, CRM namespace/name/version, ABI hash, and signature hash, but stale-route invalidation still deleted every cached entry with the same route name. A stale route for one CRM contract can now only invalidate that exact full route-contract cache entry, so another contract using the same route key keeps its cached resolution.
- Phase 100 verification after closed-loop review: the red CLI TypeScript smoke first reproduced two contracts sharing `route` being warmed into cache, then a stale route for contract A evicting contract B and forcing an unnecessary resolve. After remediation, the generated runtime smoke passed and the codegen unit test asserts `invalidateRelayRouteCache(...)` deletes by `cacheKey`.
- Phase 101 FastDB free-threading table row-read safety closed the all-in-one suite blocker found during Phase 99 verification: `Table.__iter__`, `Table.__getitem__`, `Table.iter_reuse()`, and fallback `StringColumn.get()` now serialize per-table `tryGetFeature(...)` row reads through a table-owned `RLock`, while leaving NumPy column-array access on its existing column accessor cache path. This prevents multiple Python threads from entering the same native layer row materialization path concurrently under free-threaded Python.
- Phase 101 verification after closed-loop review: the targeted free-threading concurrent table-iteration test passed 100 consecutive runs, `test_free_threading.py` passed with 12 tests, FastDB column/string/free-threading focused tests passed with 65 tests, the full FastDB Python suite passed with 597 tests, and C-Two FastDB/grid integration still passed with 56 tests. A follow-up closed-loop review found `Table.iter_reuse()` as another native row-read producer and added a mechanical lock guardrail test plus negative-index underflow protection for `Table.__getitem__`.
- Phase 101 C-Two TypeScript route contract identity guardrail closed a public bytes-transport authority bypass: generated clients normally pass the generated contract constant, but exported `createHttpRelayEncodedTransport(...)` / `createRelayAwareHttpEncodedTransport(...)` also accept application-supplied contract objects. The generated runtime now validates `schema`, non-empty CRM namespace/name/version, and lower-hex ABI/signature hashes before building expected CRM headers or resolve queries, so malformed contract identity fails locally instead of reaching relay/network code.
- Phase 101 verification after closed-loop review: the red CLI TypeScript smoke first reproduced `{ ...CONTRACT, namespace: "" }` reaching fetch and returning success. After remediation, the smoke asserts malformed route contract identity throws with a namespace diagnostic and never calls fetch, while the codegen unit test asserts the generated validator includes schema and non-empty identity field checks.
- Phase 102 FastDB Python direct-engine BOOL producer parity closed a FastDB-owned source-to-sink split that could bypass the Phase 98 bool parser outside call-db: direct `ColumnEngine` and `ObjectEngine` writes now preserve `BOOL` / `list[BOOL]` semantic field metadata and normalize producer values before C numeric/list writes, and fixed `Table.fill(...)` applies the same scalar `BOOL` parser before bulk numeric column writes while leaving ordinary `U8` fields on the numeric cast path. This keeps direct FastDB usage and C-Two call-db payload construction aligned without adding any FastDB schema parsing to C-Two core.
- Phase 102 verification after closed-loop review: red FastDB tests reproduced scalar and native-list `BOOL` string values reaching direct engine C writers as raw strings, review reproduced `ColumnEngine.push_many()` partially writing earlier rows before a later bool value failed, and a follow-up review found fixed `Table.fill(...)` still bypassed the parser for scalar `BOOL` columns. A second review found failed bool `push_many()` batches could still create empty table metadata before rejecting an invalid value, so bool batch normalization now runs before table creation while non-bool batches keep the streaming path. After the final remediation, fixed-fill and empty-table bool guardrails passed, ColumnEngine/ObjectEngine/call-db/bridge focused tests passed with 69 tests, FastDB import-boundary/ColumnEngine/ObjectEngine/schema/call-db/bridge/provider tests passed with 304 tests, and the C-Two FastDB/grid integration group passed with 57 tests after the earlier direct IPC `early eof` and an Array-to-variadic-tuple observation were both isolated as non-reproducible on focused rerun and clean full rerun. Compileall passed for touched FastDB Python files, the C-Two production fastdb-import scan found no matches, and `git diff --check` passed in both repositories; earlier broader Phase 102 evidence also included the full FastDB Python suite and full C-Two verification stack.
- Phase 103 C-Two TypeScript route path guardrail closed the matching route/method path bypass: public generated bytes transports previously allowed empty `routeName` or method names, which produced malformed HTTP paths such as empty route segments instead of failing at the SDK boundary. Generated explicit HTTP and relay-aware transports now require non-empty string `routeName` and method values before any resolve or data-plane fetch.
- Phase 103 verification after closed-loop review: the red CLI TypeScript smoke first reproduced an empty `routeName` reaching fetch. After remediation, empty `routeName` and empty method calls both throw locally with route path diagnostics and no fetch invocation across explicit HTTP and relay-aware transports, and the codegen unit test asserts both generated call paths include the route path validator. C-Two CLI contract command tests passed with 15 tests.
- Phase 104 FastDB scalar Array variadic tuple input bridge closed a resource-shape split in FastDB-owned bridge derivation: CRM `Array[Scalar]` input hooks now map to resource parameters annotated as `tuple[Scalar, ...]` or bare `tuple` by preserving item scalar coercion and returning an immutable tuple, while fixed-length tuple resource annotations, unsupported non-sequence resource annotations, nested sequence items, and non-scalar variadic tuple items fail during derivation instead of receiving a list-shaped half-bridge. C-Two remains fastdb-neutral and only executes the derived `cc.bridge(input=...)` hook across thread-local, direct IPC, and relay.
- Phase 104 verification after closed-loop review: red FastDB bridge and C-Two integration tests first reproduced `Array[I32]` input bridges passing lists to a resource annotated as `tuple[int, ...]`. Review then found adjacent bare-`tuple`, unsupported resource-annotation, and nested sequence item half-bridge risks and added coverage for them. After remediation, the focused FastDB tuple input tests passed with 4 tests, FastDB `test_c_two_bridge.py` passed with 138 tests including unsupported resource-annotation and nested sequence item guardrails, FastDB import-boundary/bridge/call-db/codegen/schema focused tests passed with 289 tests, the full FastDB Python suite passed with 605 tests, and the C-Two FastDB/grid integration group passed with 57 tests proving thread-local, direct IPC, and explicit HTTP relay all deliver tuple inputs to the resource. Compileall passed for `python/fastdb4py/c_two_bridge.py`, the C-Two production FastDB import scan found no matches, and `git diff --check` passed in both repositories.
- Phase 105 C-Two TypeScript HTTP transport boundary guardrail closed a public generated-transport authority and runtime-diagnostic gap: `createHttpRelayEncodedTransport(...)` and `createRelayAwareHttpEncodedTransport(...)` now validate transport options, base/anchor URLs, injected or global `fetch`, and user headers at construction; non-reserved custom headers still pass through explicit HTTP, relay-aware resolve, and relay-aware data-plane calls, but `Content-Type` and C-Two expected-contract headers cannot be overridden, including by case variants.
- Phase 105 verification after closed-loop review: red codegen and generated TypeScript smoke tests first reproduced missing helper generation and a reserved expected CRM header override reaching the generated transport. After remediation, focused C-Two codegen and CLI TypeScript smoke tests passed; the review loop then found missing options-object diagnostics and missing positive custom-header propagation coverage, both were added, and the same focused tests passed again.
- Phase 106 C-Two TypeScript resolve error-body transport classification closed a remaining relay-aware resolve parity gap: generated `createRelayAwareHttpEncodedTransport(...)` now treats failed reads of non-200 resolve response bodies as `C2HttpTransportError`, matching the existing successful-response resolve body-read boundary instead of converting unreadable error bodies into empty `C2HttpRelayError` values.

Bare tuple shapes use fastdb schema field order and schema scalar converters, while fixed tuple annotations keep explicit arity/item validation and variadic tuple annotations remain rejected for single-feature bridge shapes. The same review closed adjacent mapping-row annotation guardrails so explicit mapping-shaped single-feature and batch row annotations must use string keys.

- Phase 111 C-Two TypeScript relay URL authority guardrail closed the remaining generated HTTP transport URL boundary gap: public explicit base URLs, relay-aware anchor URLs, and resolve-returned `relay_url` values now pass through the same absolute HTTP(S) normalization, reject query or fragment components, strip trailing slashes, and fail before data-plane fetch can compose a malformed path. Resolve-returned URL failures are raised while normalizing resolve payload shape, preserving the control-plane diagnostic boundary instead of surfacing as a later route-ordering or data-plane error.

- Phase 112 C-Two TypeScript relay URL whitespace guardrail closed a parser-leniency gap discovered during the Phase 111 follow-up review: JavaScript `URL` accepts leading/trailing whitespace while the generated helper returned the original string, so whitespace could pass validation and still reach fetch composition. The shared relay URL normalizer now rejects any whitespace before URL parsing, covering explicit base URLs, relay-aware anchor URLs, and resolve-returned `relay_url` values.

- Phase 120 FastDB TypeScript WASM-owned payload ingress closed the first concrete zero-copy ingress gap past the existing single-copy owned-heap load: fastdb4ts can now allocate a retained WASM heap byte range, let a caller fill it, and transfer that exact pointer to native `WxDatabase.loadFromOwnedHeap(...)` without a second allocation or `HEAPU8.set(...)` copy during database load.
- Phase 120 verification after closed-loop review: red TypeScript runtime smoke first failed because `allocateFastdbOwnedBytes` was not exported. - Phase 121 FastDB TypeScript transport-owned payload surface closed the high-level runtime gap above Phase 120: `ORM.fromBuffer(...)`, `FastSerializer.loads(...)`, columnar/object-graph feature decode, and columnar/object-graph call-db decode/view now accept `FastdbOwnedBytes`, so a future C-Two TypeScript transport can pass its owned WASM response buffer through provider runtime APIs instead of losing ownership at the first `new Uint8Array(payload)` coercion.

- Phase 122 FastDB scalar bridge resource annotation guardrail closed a scalar half-bridge risk in FastDB-owned derivation: CRM scalar input/output bridges now derive only when the resource side is untyped/object-like or scalar-shaped, while mapping and sequence resource annotations fail during derivation before C-Two can register a hook that would pass scalar values into non-scalar resource code.

- Phase 124 C-Two/FastDB TypeScript provider-owned held response payload retention closed the half-implemented transport-owned payload boundary: `C2EncodedClientTransport.call(...)` can now be implemented by application/provider transports that return a provider-owned response object, codec `decode(...)` and `fromBuffer(...)` receive the same `C2ResponsePayload`, held calls expose the same object through `C2HeldResult.buffer` instead of discarding it, and FastDB generated typed facades accept C-Two's widened held buffer shape without pretending every provider-owned response is a concrete `FastdbDatabaseBytes`; built-in explicit and relay-aware HTTP transports were still byte-only subinterfaces in this slice, before the follow-up response allocator work.

- Phase 126 C-Two/FastDB TypeScript response payload allocator closed the next transport-owned ingress slice and failure guardrail: generated explicit HTTP relay and relay-aware data-plane transports accept a codec-neutral `responsePayloadAllocator`, require `Content-Length` plus a readable stream by default for successful allocated responses, write known-length stream chunks into the allocator-owned `Uint8Array` view, optionally support bounded `responsePayloadUnknownLengthStrategy: "buffer"` by snapshotting unknown-length chunks before allocating and copying into the provider-owned payload, return the allocator's provider-owned payload, release allocations on reader acquisition, invalid allocation shape, stream read, length mismatch, and invalid chunk failures, keep successful allocations retained for the caller, keep relay-aware resolve GET outside the allocator path, and preserve ordinary `Uint8Array` responses when no allocator is configured. FastDB codegen now emits `createFastdbC2ResponsePayloadAllocator(module)` so that structural C-Two hook can be backed by `FastdbOwnedBytes` / `allocateFastdbOwnedBytes(...)` without any FastDB import in C-Two-generated code.
- Phase 126 verification after closed-loop review: the red generated TypeScript CLI smoke first reproduced `getReader()` failure leaving `readerFailureReleaseCount` at `0`; review then reproduced malformed allocation shape validation leaving `malformedAllocationReleaseCount` at `0`, cleanup throwing in a way that masked the original reader failure, and unknown-length buffering that retained a reused stream chunk by reference instead of snapshotting it; follow-up smokes now cover provider-owned payload release through the same failure path, throwing cleanup that must not mask the original reader failure, missing `Content-Length`, explicit unknown-length rejection by default, unknown-length `"buffer"` allocation, reused unknown-length chunk snapshots, missing body stream without allocation, short streams, overlong streams, non-`Uint8Array` chunks, successful explicit HTTP allocation, successful relay-aware data-plane allocation, and the invariant that relay-aware resolve does not call the allocator, while generated structure coverage asserts the reader is optional, acquired inside the guarded block, performs best-effort cleanup for allocations and invalid allocation shapes on error, snapshots unknown-length chunks, and releases the stream lock in `finally`. FastDB codegen tests assert the generated allocator helper imports `allocateFastdbOwnedBytes`, returns `FastdbDatabaseBytes`, handles zero-length responses, and the C-Two grid-to-FastDB TypeScript smoke wires it into `createRelayAwareHttpEncodedTransport(...)` with `arrayBuffer()` disabled. After remediation, `cargo test --manifest-path cli/Cargo.toml --test contract_commands contract_codegen_typescript_strict_fastdb_output_compiles_with_tsc -- --nocapture` passed, `cargo test --manifest-path core/foundation/c2-codegen/Cargo.toml --test typescript` passed with 11 tests, `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py -q` in FastDB passed with 56 tests, `cargo test --manifest-path cli/Cargo.toml --test contract_commands` passed with 15 tests, `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_grid_fastdb_bridge_smoke.py::test_grid_fastdb_export_feeds_fastdb_typescript_codegen -q --timeout=60` passed, both Rust `cargo fmt --check` commands passed, `git diff --check` passed in both repositories, and the C-Two production fastdb-import scan found no matches.
- Phase 127 allocator documentation synchronization closed stale guidance in C-Two roadmap/vision and FastDB docs that still described the FastDB `FastdbOwnedBytes` response allocator adapter as future work. The docs now say the generated adapter exists, composes with C-Two allocator-backed HTTP transports, and, after Phase 128, leave only broader transport parity, more efficient unknown-length/chunked body handling beyond the buffered fallback, SDK packaging/runtime guidance, arbitrary JS-buffer zero-copy, and non-native variable-length list runtime support as future work.
- Phase 128/129 C-Two TypeScript unknown-length allocator fallback closed the explicit HTTP chunked-body strategy gap without weakening the default fast path: `responsePayloadUnknownLengthStrategy` defaults to `reject`, so allocator-backed transports still fail locally when `Content-Length` is missing unless the caller opts into `"buffer"`; the buffered fallback requires a readable body stream, snapshots each `Uint8Array` chunk before allocating to avoid reader buffer reuse corruption, enforces `responsePayloadUnknownLengthMaxBytes` with a 64 MiB default and 2_147_483_647 hard maximum before allocation, allocates exactly the final byte length, copies into the allocator view, returns the provider-owned payload, and keeps relay-aware resolve GET outside the allocator path. This is intentionally a buffered fallback rather than a zero-copy path; the FastDB zero-copy ingress target remains the known-length allocator path that writes directly into FastDB-owned WASM memory.
- Phase 128/129 verification after closed-loop review: the red generated TypeScript CLI smoke first failed because `responsePayloadUnknownLengthStrategy` was not part of `C2HttpRelayTransportOptions`, then the review loop found relay-aware coverage still used `Content-Length` and did not prove option pass-through, and the next red smoke reproduced reused reader chunks corrupting buffered unknown-length output. The max-bytes guardrail smoke then failed at TypeScript compile because `responsePayloadUnknownLengthMaxBytes` was not part of the generated transport options. After remediation, focused CLI smoke passed for explicit unknown-length buffered allocation, default missing-`Content-Length` rejection, invalid strategy rejection, bounded `responsePayloadUnknownLengthMaxBytes` rejection before allocator calls, reused-chunk snapshotting, relay-aware unknown-length pass-through, and unchanged reader/invalid-allocation failure cleanup; C-Two codegen structure tests passed with 11 tests and assert the option type, normalizer, pass-through, unknown-length helper, max-bytes guardrail, and chunk snapshot guardrail. - Phase 129 C-Two TypeScript provider-owned response release closed the adjacent failure-sink leak: generated codec transports now release provider-owned response payloads when output codec lookup fails after the wire call, ordinary `decode(...)` throws, or held `fromBuffer(...)` throws; held decode-fallback success keeps `.buffer` available but releases the retained raw provider-owned buffer on `HeldResult.release()` while leaving the materialized decoded value alone. Release during failure handling is best-effort and does not mask the original provider error.

- Phase 139 C-Two TypeScript IPC chunked response layout feasibility guardrail closes the pre-read half of the Phase 138 chunk integrity work: after the first chunk, generated assembly now proves the fixed non-final chunk size leaves at least one byte for the final chunk before reading any more frames. This rejects impossible layouts such as `total_size=5,total_chunks=2,first_chunk_bytes=5` immediately, avoids unsafe large multiplication by checking the maximum feasible non-final chunk size with division first, and prevents a malformed peer from driving an extra frame read for a layout that can never complete.

- Phase 143 C-Two TypeScript IPC request SHM writer transport closes the generated producer-side SHM frame gap without adding a built-in Node/POSIX adapter: `createIpcEncodedTransport(...)` now accepts `requestShmWriter` and `requestShmThreshold`, advertises the writer's client SHM prefix and buddy segments in the IPC handshake, writes payloads above the threshold through the injected writer, sends Rust-compatible `FLAG_CALL_V2 | FLAG_BUDDY` frames as `[buddy_payload][call_control]`, validates returned block metadata against u16/u32 wire limits and advertised segment ranges, releases invalid or failed-write blocks, closes the connection after a buddy frame write failure, leaves non-dedicated successful blocks for server-side cross-process free, releases dedicated blocks after a matching server response proves consumption, and keeps Rust server early-reject paths responsible for freeing unconsumed buddy request blocks before replying.

- Phase 144 TypeScript IPC dedicated Node/POSIX SHM helper slice keeps the generated adapter narrow and explicit: generated TypeScript exports structural Node/POSIX file-system contracts, `createNodePosixDedicatedResponseShmReader(...)`, and `createNodePosixDedicatedRequestShmWriter(...)`; the response reader only accepts dedicated SHM blocks, requires dedicated offset `0`, reads from `C2_IPC_DEDICATED_SHM_HEADER_BYTES`, and marks `read_done` during release; the request writer validates POSIX SHM prefixes against Rust's 24-byte `MemPool` prefix limit, creates page-aligned dedicated header-plus-payload segments, advertises no buddy pool segments in the client handshake, returns dedicated buddy metadata with offset `0`, and unlinks the segment during generated writer release after a matching server response. Runtime smoke covers direct dedicated response read/release, non-dedicated rejection, nonzero dedicated offset rejection, generic request-writer prefix-length rejection, direct request writer handshake/frame metadata, and request unlink after response.
- Phase 144 verification after closed-loop review: red generated TypeScript structure coverage first failed because Node/POSIX SHM helper types and factories were missing; remediation added structural file-system contracts, dedicated response/request helper factories, POSIX name/path validation, full read/write loops, page-aligned dedicated request file creation, `read_done` marking, offset-0 validation, and request writer prefix-length validation matching Rust `MemPool` prefix limits. Review against Rust `c2-mem`, `c2-ipc`, and `c2-server` confirmed dedicated payloads live after a 64-byte header, dedicated offsets must be `0`, request dedicated blocks are released by the client only after a matching response, and non-dedicated buddy support needs c2-mem allocator semantics. Final verification passed `cargo fmt --check --manifest-path core/foundation/c2-codegen/Cargo.toml`, `cargo fmt --check --manifest-path cli/Cargo.toml`, `cargo test --manifest-path core/foundation/c2-codegen/Cargo.toml --test typescript` with 11 tests, `cargo test --manifest-path cli/Cargo.toml --test contract_commands` with 15 tests, FastDB `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py -q` with 56 tests, FastDB `node --test tests/ts/test_c_two_runtime.mjs` with 45 tests, `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_grid_fastdb_bridge_smoke.py::test_grid_fastdb_export_feeds_fastdb_typescript_codegen -q --timeout=60` with 1 test, the C-Two production FastDB import scan with no matches, and `git diff --check` in both repos.
- Phase 145 TypeScript IPC SHM runtime adapter requirement freeze: the dedicated-only helper is useful for dedicated segments, fixtures, and runtimes that expose POSIX SHM as files, while generated TypeScript now also exposes structural native-buddy backend contracts and wrapper factories for non-dedicated response/read and request/write hooks. Complete non-dedicated parity still needs a concrete native or FFI-backed c2-mem-compatible backend. That backend must use POSIX SHM APIs and c2-mem-compatible allocator semantics where response non-dedicated release performs buddy `free_at` in the server pool, request non-dedicated writer allocates from a c2-mem-compatible client buddy pool and lets the Rust server free accepted blocks, and every path preserves the existing generated frame validation and provider-owned allocator ingress contract. The frozen requirements live in [`docs/plans/2026-05-20-typescript-ipc-shm-runtime-adapter-requirements.md`](2026-05-20-typescript-ipc-shm-runtime-adapter-requirements.md), which explicitly keeps FastDB at the codec/allocator layer and rejects pure TypeScript non-dedicated buddy emulation.
- Phase 145 verification after closed-loop review: the new requirement freeze doc records the current generated structural native-buddy wrappers, dedicated-only file helper limits, concrete native/FFI backend requirements, FastDB boundary, packaging direction, and future acceptance gates. Review against the live generated TypeScript and Rust `c2-mem` / `c2-ipc` / `c2-server` paths first found stale wording that ignored the existing native-buddy wrapper surface; remediation updated C-Two and FastDB docs to distinguish generated wrapper contracts from the still-missing concrete c2-mem backend. The focused CLI smoke then exposed a real generated guardrail ordering bug where a dedicated SHM response with nonzero offset could report missing server SHM prefix first; remediation moved the dedicated offset check ahead of prefix-dependent block construction so malformed dedicated metadata fails before reader invocation. Final verification passed `cargo fmt --check --manifest-path core/foundation/c2-codegen/Cargo.toml`, `cargo fmt --check --manifest-path cli/Cargo.toml`, `cargo test --manifest-path core/foundation/c2-codegen/Cargo.toml --test typescript` with 11 tests, `cargo test --manifest-path cli/Cargo.toml --test contract_commands` with 15 tests, FastDB `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py -q` with 56 tests, FastDB `node --test tests/ts/test_c_two_runtime.mjs` with 45 tests, `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_grid_fastdb_bridge_smoke.py::test_grid_fastdb_export_feeds_fastdb_typescript_codegen -q --timeout=60` with 1 test, the C-Two production FastDB import scan with no matches, and `git diff --check` in both repositories.
- Phase 146 dedicated request helper guardrail closes the local release authority gap before any full buddy backend work: generated `createNodePosixDedicatedRequestShmWriter(...)` now tracks active segment indexes created by that writer and rejects duplicate or forged `release(block)` calls before computing the unlink path, so an application cannot hand the helper an arbitrary same-prefix dedicated block and make it unlink a segment the writer did not allocate.

- Phase 148 generated native-buddy wrapper implementation closes the code/docs mismatch left by the Phase 145 requirement freeze: generated TypeScript now exports structural `C2NodePosixNativeBuddyResponseShmBackend` and `C2NodePosixNativeBuddyRequestShmBackend` contracts plus `createNodePosixNativeBuddyResponseShmReader(...)` and `createNodePosixNativeBuddyRequestShmWriter(...)`. The response wrapper passes a generated owned destination into the injected native/FFI backend and does not expose backend-owned aliases to callers; the request wrapper validates native backend POSIX prefix/segment metadata before handshake advertisement, delegates allocation to `writeRequest(...)`, delegates local cleanup to `releaseRequest(...)`, and still relies on the generated transport to leave accepted non-dedicated request blocks to Rust server free authority. Review remediation also moved dedicated offset validation to the generic generated transport boundary so dedicated response blocks with nonzero offsets never reach a reader and dedicated request blocks with nonzero offsets are locally released before any buddy frame is written.

- Phase 149 native-buddy response wrapper ownership guardrail: generated `createNodePosixNativeBuddyResponseShmReader(...)` now treats a backend that accidentally returns bytes as a copy source rather than exposing that backend-owned view, and if those returned bytes fail post-read validation it calls `releaseResponse(block)` before surfacing a transport error so the generic transport does not leak the response SHM block on wrapper-level post-read failures. - Phase 150 native-buddy non-dedicated boundary guardrail closes the accidental dedicated-lifecycle overlap in the generated wrapper factories: `createNodePosixNativeBuddyResponseShmReader(...)` now rejects dedicated response blocks before invoking the native/FFI backend, and `createNodePosixNativeBuddyRequestShmWriter(...)` now treats any backend-returned dedicated request block as invalid, releases it through `releaseRequest(...)`, and fails before a buddy call frame can be written. This keeps dedicated lifecycle on the dedicated helper or an explicit composite runtime reader/writer, while the native-buddy wrappers remain strictly for c2-mem-compatible non-dedicated buddy backends.

- Phase 152 c2-mem FFI request-buddy substrate starts the concrete native backend path without moving allocator policy into TypeScript or FastDB: generated request SHM writers now expose optional `markConsumed(block)`, generated IPC calls it after observing a server response for accepted non-dedicated request blocks, and the new `core/foundation/c2-mem-ffi` workspace crate exports a C ABI request pool over Rust `c2-mem`. The C ABI validates POSIX SHM prefixes, pre-creates the configured buddy segments for handshake advertisement, reports Rust-compatible segment names/data sizes, writes request payloads into non-dedicated buddy blocks, rejects oversized payloads rather than dedicated fallback, never returns unadvertised segment indexes, tracks local writer-owned blocks, drops local release authority for server-consumed blocks through `c2_mem_ffi_request_pool_forget_consumed(...)`, and releases only local unsent/invalid writer-owned blocks. Response-side non-dedicated read/free and the Node/Bun/Deno binding layer remain explicit follow-up work.

- Phase 153 c2-mem FFI response-buddy substrate closes the other half of the Rust-owned native backend base: `core/foundation/c2-mem-ffi` now exports a response pool C ABI that opens deterministic Rust server buddy segments from the server prefix, validates non-dedicated response ranges before copying, fills only caller-owned destination buffers, tracks successfully read blocks, releases read blocks through c2-mem `free_at(...)`, releases any still-read blocks during pool destroy as a leak guardrail, rejects release-before-read/double-release, rejects dedicated blocks, and keeps the dedicated `read_done` lifecycle out of the native-buddy response path. The remaining concrete adapter work is the Node/Bun/Deno binding layer and generated TypeScript end-to-end composition over the C ABI.
- Phase 153 verification after closed-loop review: red response-pool tests first failed because the response read/release ABI surface was missing, then a stronger release-authority assertion showed that a released server buddy block could still be freed again through `MemPool::free_at(...)` after buddy merge, and the destroy-path review found that read-but-unreleased blocks would leak on pool destroy. Remediation implemented lazy peer segment opening and read/release authority over `MemPool`, added response range, release-authority, and destroy-cleanup coverage, and fixed the lower-level `BuddyAllocator` ancestor-free double-free detection so repeated `free_at` of a merged child cannot corrupt allocator accounting. The response helper creates and caches response pools by server SHM prefix, resolves segment size from the server handshake unless configured explicitly, rejects release-before-read so release cannot create a fresh pool for an unread block, and exposes terminal `close()` for cached pool teardown. This keeps generated code deterministic and FastDB-neutral while giving future Node/Bun/Deno bindings a stable composition point over the C ABI.

- Phase 182 generated TypeScript response allocator-failure cleanup closes a real response-SHM leak boundary: `readIpcShmSuccessPayload(...)` now releases the IPC response block if `responsePayloadAllocator(...)` throws or returns an invalid allocation before any response read occurs, and reports allocator failure unless that cleanup release also fails. The generated c2-mem-ffi response helper now opens the prefix pool during `release(...)`, and the Rust `c2_mem_ffi_response_pool_release(...)` ABI now permits release of a valid unread non-dedicated server block while preserving double-release rejection and read-tracked drop cleanup. The grid FastDB real-IPC smoke covers this with a fresh response reader whose pool cache is empty, proving the failure path performs no response read, releases the real Rust response block exactly once, marks the accepted request block consumed, and leaves local request release untouched.

- Phase 251 focused review froze these invariants: WSTR/BYTES field coercion and raw-payload storage must stay owned by FastDB rather than C-Two core; thread-local calls alone are not proof because they can hide native serializer and SWIG typemap failures; direct IPC and relay must both use the same provider-owned call-db payload and bridge output hook; held output must expose `FastdbCallView.table('return_0')` row iteration and column access for WSTR/BYTES fields without falling back to pickle; BYTES remains limited to the existing single raw-payload field model; StringColumn/BytesColumn creation must preserve the existing column accessor cache lock; and C-Two production code must remain fastdb-neutral. Source evidence covers FastDB SWIG typemaps for `const wchar_t *`, `const uchar_t *`, `uchar_t *`, and bytes-like `(const u8* data, size_t size)`, FastDB `_coerce_scalar_value(...)`, `_python_converter_for_annotation(...)`, WSTR/BYTES reader and column wrappers, FastDB `test_call_db_output_wstr_and_bytes_batch_round_trip_and_view`, and C-Two `test_fastdb_derived_bridge_maps_wstr_and_bytes_feature_output_across_transports`.
- Phase 251 verification after red/green focused review passed FastDB focused `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_call_db.py::test_call_db_output_wstr_and_bytes_batch_round_trip_and_view -q` with 1 test, FastDB focused bridge `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_bridge.py::test_derive_bridge_hooks_maps_wstr_and_bytes_aliases -q` with 1 test, C-Two focused `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_fastdb_codec_provider_smoke.py::test_fastdb_derived_bridge_maps_wstr_and_bytes_feature_output_across_transports -q --timeout=120` with 1 test, FastDB adjacent `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_call_db.py -k "wstr or bytes or table_view or output_view" -q` with 5 selected tests, FastDB string/column adjacent `uv run pytest tests/python/test_string_column.py tests/python/test_column_engine.py -k "string or bytes or wstr" -q` with 29 selected tests, C-Two adjacent `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_fastdb_codec_provider_smoke.py -k "wstr or blob or bytes" -q --timeout=120` with 1 selected test, full related FastDB `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_bridge.py tests/python/test_c_two_call_db.py -q` with 254 tests, full C-Two provider smoke `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_fastdb_codec_provider_smoke.py -q --timeout=120` with 116 tests, compileall for the touched Python files in both repos, `git diff --check` in both repos, and a C-Two production FastDB import scan over `sdk/python/src`, `core`, and `cli` with no matches. The red runs before remediation reproduced native WSTR serialization failure, bytes-like producer rejection, WSTR deserialization as non-string/`None`, and held table column access falling through to a missing fixed native column.

- Phase 252 FastDB-native no-op bridge identity guardrail closes the verification gap behind the FastDB-native resource invariant: if the CRM contract and resource method annotations are already the same FastDB ABI, FastDB bridge derivation must return `bridge == {}` and C-Two must still carry the provider-owned call-db payload through thread-local, direct IPC, explicit relay, and held output views. The provider smoke now returns distinct rows from each `active()` call and asserts the exact resource-boundary call sequence so a hidden bridge, stale result, or skipped remote call cannot satisfy the test accidentally.
- Phase 252 focused review froze these invariants: same-FastDB-ABI resource methods stay bridge-free through FastDB `_same_fastdb_abi_annotation(...)`; C-Two may register an empty bridge map but must not require a resource bridge for FastDB-native resources; ordinary calls and `cc.hold(...)` both use the provider-owned call-db transferables; direct IPC remains relay-independent before explicit relay registration; C-Two production code remains FastDB-neutral; and the Phase 251 WSTR/BYTES held-column remediation remains necessary because no-op bridge verification re-runs exposed the stable held-column failure while intermittent direct IPC `early eof` failures passed on single-test rerun.
- Phase 252 verification after focused review/remediation passed `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_fastdb_codec_provider_smoke.py::test_fastdb_native_resource_uses_empty_bridge_across_transports -q --timeout=120` with 1 test; FastDB owner-side focused `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_bridge.py::test_derive_bridge_hooks_skips_fastdb_native_resource_methods -q` with 1 test; C-Two adjacent `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_fastdb_codec_provider_smoke.py -k "native_resource or provider_payloads" -q --timeout=120` with 3 selected tests and 112 deselected; FastDB adjacent `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_bridge.py -k "native_resource or fastdb_native" -q` with 1 selected test and 187 deselected; post-review focused reruns `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_call_db.py::test_call_db_output_wstr_and_bytes_batch_round_trip_and_view -q` with 1 test and `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_fastdb_codec_provider_smoke.py::test_fastdb_derived_bridge_maps_wstr_and_bytes_feature_output_across_transports sdk/python/tests/integration/test_fastdb_codec_provider_smoke.py::test_fastdb_native_resource_uses_empty_bridge_across_transports -q --timeout=120` with 2 tests; full related FastDB `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_call_db.py tests/python/test_c_two_bridge.py -q` with 254 tests; full C-Two fastdb smoke `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_fastdb_codec_provider_smoke.py -q --timeout=120` with 116 tests; and compileall for the touched C-Two smoke and FastDB column files.

- Phase 253 downstream fastdb4ts WSTR/BYTES retained-column runtime guardrail closes the TypeScript sink behind the Phase 251 Python/C-Two WSTR/BYTES bridge fix: generated or hand-built `org.fastdb.call-db` columnar batch outputs with `WSTR` and a single `BYTES` feature field now encode, decode, and expose explicit-close retained table rows and `table.column.<field>` access in fastdb4ts without treating WSTR as STR or forcing variable-length fields through the numeric `StridedColumn` path.
- Phase 253 focused review froze these invariants: FastDB owns WSTR/BYTES runtime behavior and C-Two must continue to see only opaque provider bytes; the WASM binding must expose real wide-string setter/getter methods for both build and read paths; materialized decode and retained view must agree for WSTR and single-BYTES fields; retained numeric column access must keep the existing strided fast path while WSTR/BYTES columns use a row-backed source; object-graph scalar read/write must use the same WSTR primitives; multiple-`BYTES` and unsupported list metadata guardrails remain unchanged; and stale FastDB quality docs must not continue to claim WSTR read support is deferred. Source evidence covers FastDB `ts/embind/fastdb4ts.cpp`, `ts/fastdb4ts/src/wasm-loader.ts`, `ts/fastdb4ts/src/feature.ts`, `ts/fastdb4ts/src/orm.ts`, `ts/fastdb4ts/src/c-two.ts`, `tests/ts/test_c_two_runtime.mjs`, and `ts/analysis/QUALITY_AUDIT.md`.
- Phase 253 verification after focused review/remediation passed FastDB `npm --prefix ts/fastdb4ts run build`, focused `node --test --test-name-pattern "WSTR and bytes batch outputs" tests/ts/test_c_two_runtime.mjs` with 1 test using non-ASCII WSTR values, FastDB Python codegen `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py -q` with 57 tests, full fastdb4ts `npm --prefix ts/fastdb4ts run test:ts` with 74 tests, C-Two generated FastDB TypeScript smoke `C2_RELAY_ANCHOR_ADDRESS= uv run pytest sdk/python/tests/integration/test_grid_fastdb_bridge_smoke.py::test_grid_fastdb_export_feeds_fastdb_typescript_codegen -q --timeout=120` with 1 test, `git diff --check` in both repositories, a C-Two production FastDB import scan over `sdk/python/src`, `core`, and `cli` with no matches, and a FastDB stale-deferred-WSTR doc scan with no matches. The red focused run before remediation reproduced `decoded[0].name` as an empty string instead of `"123"`, proving the old TypeScript/WASM path read WSTR through the wrong binding.

- Phase 254 fastdb4ts object-graph WSTR/BYTES row-runtime guardrail closes the adjacent sink found during Phase 253 review: object-graph call-db feature batches with `WSTR` and a single `BYTES` raw-payload field now materialize and expose retained rows with the same values, while object-graph retained views still reject column access because that profile is row/object oriented.
- Phase 254 focused review found a real implementation gap: object-graph payload construction always configured layers as Point/Tx32 before writing rows, so `setGeometryRaw(...)` for BYTES fields emitted native geometry warnings and read back point bytes instead of the raw payload. Remediation routes feature types with exactly one BYTES field to raw/Any geometry, keeps ordinary object-graph feature tables on Point/Tx32, and adds the matching multiple-BYTES guardrail to object-graph feature runtime validation so the single raw-payload slot cannot be aliased.
- Phase 254 verification after red/green remediation passed FastDB `npm --prefix ts/fastdb4ts run build`; focused `node --test --test-name-pattern "object-graph call-db runtime exposes WSTR" tests/ts/test_c_two_runtime.mjs` with 1 test; focused `node --test --test-name-pattern "multiple bytes fields" tests/ts/test_c_two_runtime.mjs` with 1 test; full fastdb4ts `npm --prefix ts/fastdb4ts run test:ts` with 75 tests; FastDB Python codegen `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py -q` with 57 tests; `git diff --check` in both repositories; and a C-Two production FastDB import scan over `sdk/python/src`, `core`, and `cli` with no matches. The red run before remediation reproduced raw BYTES reading as point-geometry bytes `[0,0,1,0,0,0,0,0]` instead of the expected payload.

- Phase 255 generated TypeScript helper WSTR/BYTES object-graph sink guardrail closes the source-to-sink gap after Phase 254: hand-built runtime bindings were proven, but generated helpers also need to emit `WSTR`/`BYTES` feature classes, object-graph call-db binding metadata, decode-only held typings, registry capability behavior, and a runnable smoke over non-ASCII WSTR plus BYTES rows.
- Phase 255 focused review found a test/support gap rather than a production code defect: generated-helper coverage had object-graph scalar/array smoke and raw feature BYTES structure tests, but no generated object-graph call-db smoke for `Batch[Feature]` containing WSTR and BYTES. The first new smoke also clarified the API boundary that retained `FastdbC2CallDbView.table(...).get(...)` is typed as base `Feature`, so user code or generated facades must cast row views while typed client materialized returns stay strongly typed.
- Phase 255 verification passed focused `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py::test_c_two_typescript_generated_object_graph_call_db_wstr_bytes_helpers_compile_and_run -q` with 1 test after the row-view cast correction, and full FastDB codegen `uv run pytest tests/python/test_c_two_codegen.py -q` with 58 tests. The generated smoke builds fastdb4ts, compiles the generated helper with `tsc`, runs Node encode/decode/view assertions for non-ASCII WSTR and BYTES, proves object-graph retained column access remains rejected, and proves the registry does not expose `fromBuffer` for a decode-only object-graph codec.

## Follow-Up Backlog

1. Broader TypeScript real IPC coverage and publishable SDK packaging: turn the initial Node/POSIX `c2-mem-ffi` direct IPC grid proof into packageable runtime coverage with its own install, build, smoke, and failure-mode matrix.
2. Bun/Deno or equivalent loader coverage: validate the same Rust-owned C ABI substrates outside Node/POSIX rather than adding generated TypeScript allocator logic.
3. TypeScript runtime support for non-native variable-length layouts: keep current semantic-only guardrails until FastDB has concrete storage/runtime support and source-to-sink tests.
4. Arbitrary bridge synthesis: treat unsupported resource shapes as a new design problem with separate derivation rules and negative diagnostics rather than adding aliases to already-covered families.
5. Lower-level fixed-table or heap-backed writes: only enter this path after benchmarks prove it beats the current mutable bulk append path for C-Two call-db batch shapes.

## Non-Goals

Do not make C-Two core parse fastdb schemas, engine profiles, table layouts, native enum values, or object-graph closure rules.

Do not treat Arrow, custom codecs, or other provider families as the portable cross-language CRM path for this workstream. They may remain optional Python/example providers, but fastdb is the required portable ABI for the CRM/codegen path described here.

Do not require existing resource classes to become CRM classes. The bridge exists precisely so resource implementations can remain domain-shaped while CRM contracts become fastdb-shaped.

Do not silently convert a partially fastdb method into a portable method. A method is portable only when both input and output have valid fastdb call-db refs, except for methods with no payload in one direction.
